Okay, here are the Human Performance and Limitations tests in the questionnaire format.

🧠 Human Performance and Limitations Test 1

1. Smoking reduces the blood's ability to carry oxygen because: A. the inspiratory tract becomes obstructed B. CO2 takes a larger lung volume C. haemoglobin has a greater affinity for CO D. CO gets trapped in the alveoli and restricts internal respiration Correct Answer: C

2. If someone is hyperventilating, the blood contains too much: A. acid B. alkaline C. CO2 D. haemoglobin Correct Answer: A (Note: Hyperventilation blows off CO2, leading to respiratory alkalosis - less acid/more alkaline. The checkmark is next to A, which indicates too much acid is the result of the body's compensatory mechanisms, or the question/checkmark might be incorrect. Standard understanding is it leads to alkalosis/less acid).

3. Accidents are caused by lack of: A. good judgment B. safe maintenance of aircraft C. interpersonal relations D. physical and mental skills Correct Answer: A

4. Blood from the pulmonary artery is? A. Rich in oxygen and low in carbon dioxide B. Rich in oxygen and rich in carbon dioxide C. Low in oxygen and low in carbon dioxide D. Low in oxygen and rich in carbon dioxide Correct Answer: D

5. Which instrument, which was introduced in the 1980s, led to the greatest reduction of accidents? A. SSR B. DME C. GPWS D. TCAS Correct Answer: C

6. When blood pressure is measured during an aviation medical examination, the pressure is: A. the venous pressure B. the pressure of O2 in the blood C. the pressure in all of the blood vessels, being representative of the pressure over the whole body D. arterial pressure in the upper arm, being equivalent to that of the heart Correct Answer: D

7. A pilot should consult an aviation medicine specialist before donating blood because: A. donation may lead to a rise in blood pressure (hypertension) B. donation may lead to a lowering of blood pressure (hypotension) C. donation may lead to a reduced tolerance of altitude D. donation may lead to a lowering of the body temperature causing unpredictable sleepiness Correct Answer: C

8. A person is suffering from hyperventilation, his blood becomes: A. more acid B. more alkaline C. more saturated with CO2 D. less saturated with oxygen Correct Answer: B

9. The amount of oxygen carried by the blood depends on: A. the partial pressure of oxygen only B. the haemoglobin only C. the amount of oxygen dissolved in the blood plasma D. the partial pressure of oxygen and the amount of haemoglobin Correct Answer: D

10. Haemoglobin is: A. dissolved in the blood B. in red blood cells C. in white cells of the blood D. in the platelets Correct Answer: B

11. The pressoreceptors have signalled low blood pressure. The body's response is to: 1. increase rate of breathing 2. increase cardiac output 3. increase heart rate 4. relax of the blood vessels 5. decrease heart rate 6. tighten of the blood vessels A. 1, 2, 3 and 4 B. 2, 3 and 6 C. 4 and 5 only D. 1, 3 and 4 Correct Answer: B

12. The body gets its energy from: 1. minerals 2. carbohydrates 3. protein 4. vitamins A. 1 & 4 only B. 2 & 3 only C. 1, 2 & 4 D. 3 & 4 only Correct Answer: B

13. What is the carcinogenic substance in cigarettes that can modify cells and cause cancer? A. Tar B. Nicotine C. Carbon monoxide D. Lead Correct Answer: A

14. Having given blood a pilot should see a doctor because of the increased susceptibility to: A. hypoxia B. low blood pressure C. hyperventilation D. Decompression sickness (DCS) Correct Answer: A

15. With a pulse rate of 72 beats a minute and a stroke volume of 70 ml, what is the cardiac output? A. 8 litres a minute B. 6 litres a minute C. 5 litres a minute D. 7 litres a minute Correct Answer: C (Calculation: 72 beats/min * 70 ml/beat = 5040 ml/min ≈ 5 L/min)

16. Who is responsible for Air Safety? A. Aircrew and Groundcrew B. Aircrew, Groundcrew and Management C. Everyone involved D. Aircrew only Correct Answer: C

17. Having donated blood aircrew should: A. rest supine for at least 1 hour, drink plenty of fluids and not fly for 48 hours B. rest supine for about 15 - 20 minutes, drink plenty of fluids and not fly for 24 hours C. aircrew are prohibited from donating blood D. aircrew are not encouraged to give blood Correct Answer: B

18. Human factors have been statistically proved to contribute approximately: A. 50% of aircraft accidents B. 70% of aircraft accidents C. 90% of aircraft accidents D. have not played a significant role in aircraft accidents Correct Answer: B

19. The oxygen-carrying capacity of a smoker who smokes 20 to 30 cigarettes a day is reduced by approximately: A. 8 - 10% B. 12 - 18% C. 20 - 25% D. 0.2 - 2% Correct Answer: A

20. The blood of the pulmonary vein is: A. rich in oxygen and lacking in CO2 B. rich in oxygen and rich in CO2 C. lacking in oxygen and rich in CO2 D. lacking in oxygen and lacking in CO2 Correct Answer: A

🧠 Human Performance and Limitations Test 2

1. Decompression sickness (DCS) is caused by: A. oxygen coming out of solution B. carbon dioxide coming out of solution C. nitrogen coming out of solution D. carbon monoxide coming out of solution Correct Answer: C

2. Which of the following is true with respect to the cause of decompression sickness? A. altitudes above 18000 ft in an unpressurized aircraft B. altitudes above 5000 ft C. climbing at more than 500 ft/min to altitude greater than 18000 ft D. temperatures greater than 24C at altitudes of over 2000 ft Correct Answer: A

3. What chemical substance in tobacco causes addiction? A. Tar and nicotine B. Tar and carbon monoxide C. Nicotine and carbon monoxide D. Nicotine Correct Answer: D

4. The contents of exhaled air compared to inhaled air will contain: A. Less N2 B. More O2 C. Less CO2 D. Less O2 Correct Answer: D

5. Which of the following factors decrease resistance to decompression sickness? 1. Body height 2. Scuba diving 3. Obesity 4. Age A. 1, 2 and 4 B. 3 and 4 C. 1, 2 and 3 D. 2, 3 and 4 Correct Answer: D

6. Blood pressure depends on the: A. resistance and the efficiency of the cells B. cardiac input and the resistance of the capillaries C. cell output and the thinness of the blood D. cardiac output and the resistance of the capillaries Correct Answer: D

7. Time of useful consciousness (TUC) following loss of pressurization at 35000 ft is: A. 3 - 4 minutes B. 5 minutes upwards C. 30 - 60 seconds D. 10 - 15 seconds Correct Answer: C

8. Dalton's Law is associated with: A. Decompression sickness (DCS) B. bends C. creeps D. hypoxia Correct Answer: D

9. Among the symptoms of hypoxia are: 1. impaired judgment 2. fast and heavy breathing 3. impairment of vision 4. muscular impairment A. 1 & 3 B. 1, 3 and 4 C. 1, 2 and 4 D. 1, 2, 3 and 4 Correct Answer: D

10. The composition of the atmosphere at 21000 ft is approximately: A. 78% He, 21% O2 and 1% CO B. 78% He, 21% O2 and 0.003% CO2 + traces C. 78% N, 21% O2 and 1% CO2 + traces D. 78% N, 21% O2 and 1% CO + traces Correct Answer: C (Note: Atmospheric composition percentages remain relatively constant with altitude, but partial pressures decrease. Option C shows the standard sea-level composition percentages, which is the likely intended answer despite the altitude context).

11. Boyle's Law has a role to play in: A. hypoxia with increased altitude B. Decompression sickness C. gastrointestinal tract barotrauma D. night vision Correct Answer: C

12. Which is the following actions is the most efficient to accelerate the release of Carbon Monoxide from the blood? A. Inhalation of pressurised oxygen B. Inhalation of a mixture of unpressurized oxygen and air C. Inhalation of pressurised carbon dioxide D. Inhalation of a mixture of unpressurized carbon dioxide and air Correct Answer: A

13. A pilot suffering from hyperventilation during final approach in poor weather can combat the effects by: A. going on 100% oxygen and go around B. slowing the breathing rate, breathing into a paper bag and continuing the approach C. increasing the rate of breathing and continuing the approach D. increasing the depth of breathing and going around Correct Answer: B

14. What is the normal tidal volume? A. 750 ml B. 500 ml C. 150 ml D. 250 ml Correct Answer: B

15. Circulation of the blood is for: 1. transportation of oxygen to the cells of the body 2. withdrawal of the waste products from the cells 3. convey nutrients to the cells A. 1 and 2 B. 2 and 3 C. 1 and 3 D. 1, 2 and 3 Correct Answer: D

16. Which of the following is correct concerning O2 and blood? A. Arterial blood is darker than venous blood B. Blood plasma is oxygenated at the heart C. Diffusion of oxygen from the alveoli to the blood is not dependent on the partial pressure D. Diffusion from the blood to the cells is dependent on the partial pressure of oxygen Correct Answer: D

17. Which of the following symptoms marks the beginning of hyperventilation? A. Slow heart beat B. Cyanosis C. Dizzy feeling D. Slow rate of breath Correct Answer: C

18. A few hours after landing a pilot feels pain in his/her joints. The correct action is: A. take exercise which will cause the pain to disappear B. take physiotherapy C. see an aviation medical specialist as soon as possible D. ignore it since is probably due to common after-effect of height Correct Answer: C

19. What law governs the oxygen transfer at the alveoli? A. Boyle's B. Charles' C. Henry's D. Gas Diffusion Law - Fick's Law Correct Answer: D

20. Carbon Monoxide: A. can have a severe affect on a pilot's abilities when receiving exposure for a relatively short period of time B. does not have an effect when the body becomes used to the gas over a long period of time C. has no effect on the human body D. is not toxic Correct Answer: A

🧠 Human Performance and Limitations Test 3

1. The partial pressure of carbon dioxide in the lungs is: A. lower than the partial pressure of CO2 in the atmosphere B. higher than the pressure of CO2 in the blood C. lower than the pressure of CO2 in the blood D. almost equal to the pressure of CO2 in the atmosphere Correct Answer: C

2. The Critical Zone of hypoxia begins at: A. 18000 ft B. 20000 ft C. 23000 ft D. 3600 ft Correct Answer: B

3. Which of the following are defined in the ICAO Standard Atmosphere? 1. Pressure 2. Temperature 3. Density 4. Humidity A. 1, 2 & 4 B. 1 & 2 C. 2, 3 & 4 D. 1, 2 & 3 Correct Answer: D

4. In an ascent, where is the greatest pressure differential? A. 0 - 5000 ft B. 5000 - 10000 ft C. 10000 - 15000 ft D. 40000 - 45000 ft Correct Answer: A

5. DCS symptoms can occur: A. when flying from an area if high pressure to an area of low pressure in an unpressurized aircraft B. when cabin pressure surges below 18000 ft C. following loss of cabin pressure at altitudes higher than 18000 ft D. emergency descent following decompression below 10000 ft Correct Answer: C

6. Under normal conditions, external respiration is a subconscious process that occurs at a rate of: A. 20 to 30 breaths/min, averaging 25 breaths/minute B. 30 to 40 breaths/min, averaging 35 breaths/minute C. 15 to 25 breaths/min, averaging 20 breaths/minute D. 12 to 20 breaths/min, averaging 16 breaths/minute Correct Answer: D

7. Which of the following statements are correct?: Decompression sickness can be avoided by: 1. staying below 18000 ft 2. maintaining cabin pressure below 8000 ft 3. breathing 100% oxygen 30 minutes prior to and during flight above 18000 ft 4. breathing 100% oxygen 60 minutes prior to and during flight above 18000 ft A. 1, 2 & 3 B. 2, 3 & 4 C. 1, 3 & 4 D. 1, 2 & 4 Correct Answer: A

8. Hyperventilation results in: A. Increased pCO2 in the blood B. Decreased pCO2 in the blood C. Increased pO2 in the blood D. Decreased pO2 in the blood Correct Answer: B

9. Time of useful consciousness at 25,000 feet with moderate activity and rapid decompression is approximately: A. 2 minutes B. 30 seconds to 5 minutes C. 2.5 minutes to 6 minutes D. 5 to 10 minutes Correct Answer: A

10. At what altitude is pressure half that at MSL: A. 8000 ft B. 10000 ft C. 18000 ft D. 36000 ft Correct Answer: C

11. Hyperventilation can cause: A. too much oxygen to the brain B. spasms in the muscles and possible unconsciousness C. bluish tinge under the nails of the fingers and the lobes of the ears D. a feeling of euphoria Correct Answer: B

12. As the body ascends, the partial pressure of oxygen within the lungs: A. decreases at a rate of 3 times the atmospheric rate B. decreases at the same rate as that of the atmosphere C. stays the same D. increases Correct Answer: B

13. The following are features of hypoxia: 1. blue discolouration of the lips and fingernails 2. shortness of breath and dizziness 3. impaired decision making and poor coordination 4. a feeling of well being A. 2, 3 and 4 are correct B. 1, 2 and 4 are correct C. 1, 3 and 4 are correct D. 1, 2 and 3 are correct Correct Answer: B (Note: Impaired decision making (3) is a symptom, but the checkmark is B. Euphoria/well-being (4) is also a symptom. Shortness of breath (2) and cyanosis (1) are symptoms. B includes 1, 2, 4. This might indicate an error in the source checkmark or question.)

14. On expiration there is: A. higher CO2 content than on intake B. more oxygen content than on intake C. less water vapour content than on intake D. the same CO2 content as on intake Correct Answer: A

15. You have been scuba diving below 10 m. When can you next fly: A. after 12 hours B. after 24 hours C. after 48 hours D. whenever you wish Correct Answer: B

16. Concerning hypoxia, why is it more hazardous if flying solo? A. The effects are increased B. It is difficult to recognize the first symptoms of hypoxia for a pilot in initial training C. It is more difficult to manage the oxygen systems on your own D. There is no one to take control once the symptoms of hypoxia appear Correct Answer: B

17. Which of the following statements, if any, are correct? 1. Euphoria is a possible result of hypoxia 2. Euphoria can lead to degradation in pilots performance A. 1 only is correct B. 2 only is correct C. Both 1 and 2 are correct D. Neither Correct Answer: C

18. Short-term memory impairment occurs at what height? A. 8000 ft B. 12000 ft C. 15000 ft D. 18000 ft Correct Answer: B

19. 100% oxygen without pressure can be used up to: A. 50000 ft B. 40000 ft C. 60000 ft D. 70000 ft Correct Answer: B

20. TUC (time of useful consciousness) is dependent upon: 1. rate of decompression 2. altitude of the occurrence 3. type of aircraft 4. activity of the pilot 5. personal health A. 1, 2 & 3 B. all of the above C. all except 3 D. 2, 3 & 5 Correct Answer: C

🧠 Human Performance and Limitations Test 4

1. A person suffering from glaucoma will have: A. cloudiness of the lens B. cloudiness of the cornea C. increased pressure of the eye D. colour blindness Correct Answer: C

2. The most dangerous type of incapacitation is: A. acute B. rapid C. insidious D. none of the above Correct Answer: C

3. What is a stereotype and involuntary reaction to a stimulation? A. Data control B. A reflex C. Stimulation control D. Automatic stimulation Correct Answer: B

4. Glaucoma is caused by: A. excess pressure within the eye B. a clouding of the lens C. damage to the cornea D. damage to the retina Correct Answer: A

5. While turning the aircraft the pilots moves his/her head. What effect might the pilot be exposed to: A. Coriolis Effect B. Somatogravic Effect C. Flicker Effect D. Oculogravic Effect Correct Answer: A

6. Which Law is relevant to decompression sickness? A. Boyles Law B. Henrys Law C. The Combined Gas Law D. Daltons Law Correct Answer: B

7. Good quality sunglasses provide: A. the ability to react to varying light levels automatically B. good luminance characteristics, avoidance of glare and harsh shadows, protection against UV and IR and equal absorption of colours C. for the pilots individual needs D. no distortion of aircraft windscreens Correct Answer: D

8. On initiating recovery from a spin, the pilot may have a strong sensation of turning: A. in a direction opposite to that of the spin B. in a direction the same as the spin C. slowly upwards D. quickly upwards Correct Answer: A

9. Barotrauma of the middle ear is caused by differences between the pressures in the: A. inner ear and middle ear B. ambient air and the middle ear C. outer ear D. semicircular canals Correct Answer: B

10. Night flying at 10000 ft you find that your acuity decreases. What can you do about it to improve your acuity? A. Use your peripheral vision B. Go onto oxygen C. Turn up the instrument lights D. Switch on or turn up the cabin heat Correct Answer: B

11. What actions should a pilot take if suffering from vertigo? 1. Check and cross-check the aircraft instruments 2. Accept and ignore illusions 3. Keep head movements to a minimum 4. Believe the aircraft instruments A. 1, 2 and 3 B. 2, 3 and 4 C. 1, 3 and 4 D. 1, 2, 3 and 4 Correct Answer: D

12. The function of the retina is to: A. convert light images into meaningful information B. transport electrical impulses to the brain C. convert light signals into electrical impulses D. convert light signals into chemical impulses Correct Answer: C

13. The metabolism of alcohol is: A. influenced by time B. accelerated by drinking coffee C. quicker when the body gets used to alcohol D. improved by the use of easy-to-get medication Correct Answer: A

14. Vertigo can be caused by a blocked eustachian tube. A. True B. False Correct Answer: A

15. What is the residual volume? A. 70 ml B. 500 ml C. 350 ml D. 1200 ml Correct Answer: D

16. Vertigo causes the illusion when flying of: A. flying straight while in a spin B. climbing while turning C. a tumbling or turning sensation associated sometimes with dizziness D. descending with a decrease of speed Correct Answer: C

17. Perceptual conflict between the vestibular apparatus and the visual sensory inputs: 1. can occur when flying IMC and may be compelling 2. can cause attitude misinformation 3. may occur when taking off bank following a sustained turn 4. can occur when decelerating A. 1, 2 and 3 B. 2, 3 and 4 C. 1, 3 and 4 D. 1, 2, 3 and 4 Correct Answer: D

18. The eye can adjust to: A. high levels of illumination in 10 minutes and darkness in 30 minutes B. high levels of illumination in 10 seconds and darkness in 30 minutes C. high levels of illumination in 30 minutes and darkness in 10 minutes D. high levels of illumination in 30 minutes and darkness in 10 seconds Correct Answer: B

19. Disorientation is most likely to occur when: 1. flying IMC 2. the pilot is distracted (using FMS for example) 3. flying from IMC to VMC 4. the pilot is unwell or fatigued A. 1, 2 and 3 B. 1, 2, 3 and 4 C. 1, 2 and 4 D. 2, 3 & 4 Correct Answer: C

20. When the visual image is focused in front of the retina the condition is: A. myopia B. hypermetropia C. presbycusis D. astigmatism Correct Answer: A

🧠 Human Performance and Limitations Test 5

1. What is the relationship between stress and fatigue? A. No stress and no fatigue is good B. All stress and fatigue is good C. Stress can be good, fatigue is always bad D. No stress and some fatigue is good Correct Answer: C

2. Which of the following are correct? 1. Scuba diving imposes no restriction on flying 2. Use of some medication can affect flying 3. One should drink sufficient water during flight to prevent dehydration 4. Diet does not have an effect on health A. 2 & 3 B. 1, 2 & 3 C. 2, 3 & 4 D. 1, 2, 3 & 4 Correct Answer: A

3. A person that is exposed to extreme or prolonged stress factors can perceive: A. distress B. eustress C. coping stress D. stressors Correct Answer: A

4. Stimuli must be of a certain strength for them to be detected. This strength is known as: A. sensory limitation B. sensory threshold C. sensory strength D. sensory volume Correct Answer: B

5. The sequence of GAS (General Adaptation Syndrome) is: A. alarm resistance exhaustion B. resistance exhaustion alarm C. alarm flight exhaustion D. exhaustion resistance alarm Correct Answer: A

6. What will happen to the body when in situations of extreme heat? 1. Shivering 2. Vasoconstriction of the exterior blood vessels 3. Sweating 4. Vasodilation of the exterior blood vessels A. 1, 2, 3 and 4 B. 2 and 3 only C. 1 and 2 only D. 3 and 4 only Correct Answer: D

7. Extreme cold may be associated with: A. aggression B. aggression and anxiety C. anxiety D. contentment or apathy Correct Answer: D

8. Performance can be increased by: A. putting a student pilot under stress B. a moderate amount of stress C. no stress at all if possible D. ignoring stress as all good pilots leave stress on the ground Correct Answer: B

9. If in a state of stress which is impossible to overcome, the pilot will be in a state of: A. eustress B. hypertension C. distress D. regression Correct Answer: C

10. Should a pilot fly with a bad cold, he/she could suffer from: A. chokes B. bends C. sinus pain D. blurred vision Correct Answer: C

11. Stressors are: A. external factors only B. internal factors only C. both external and internal factors D. neither external nor internal factors Correct Answer: C

12. A person suffering from extreme cold will stop shivering and thereafter become colder and colder when the internal body falls to about: A. 20C B. 25C C. 30C D. 35C Correct Answer: D

13. Tuned resonance of the body parts, distressing the individual can be caused by: A. acceleration along the horizontal flight path B. resonance between 150 - 250 Hz C. resonance between 16 - 18 GHz D. resonance between 1 - 100 Hz Correct Answer: D

14. According to the "General Adaptation Syndrome" which of the following statement(s) is/are correct? 1. During the alarm phase adrenalin will cause a large release of glucose into the blood, a raised heartbeat and blood pressure plus an increase in the rate and depth of breathing 2. During the resistance phase the parasympathetic system releases cortisol helping in the conversion of fat into sugar 3. During the exhaustion phase the body has to be given time to eliminate the waste products which have been generated excessively A. 1 & 2 only are correct B. 2 & 3 only are correct C. 1, 2 & 3 are correct D. only 1 is correct Correct Answer: C

15. Even with a small ingestion of alcohol: A. the brain will be stimulated thereby increasing the resistance to hypoxia B. the brain functions will be increased thereby increasing performance at high altitudes C. the pilot will remain unaffected D. the pilot's performance will be degraded Correct Answer: D

16. The effects of vibration are greatest: A. at high altitudes B. at low altitudes C. in smooth air D. when fatigued Correct Answer: D

17. Cognitive appraisal: A. occurs only with negative events B. is the objective evaluation of a situation and the perceived ability to cope with it C. is the subjective evaluation of a situation and the perceived ability to cope with it D. depends on the individual's arousal Correct Answer: C

18. The body loses water via: A. the skin, lungs and kidneys B. the skin C. the skin, lungs and liver D. the skin, liver and kidneys Correct Answer: A

19. At height cockpit humidity can be between: A. 20 - 25 % B. 40 - 60 % C. 30 - 60% D. 5 - 15 % Correct Answer: D

20. What is the relationship between stress and performance when plotted on a graph? A. The relationship is linear B. The relationship is exponential C. There is no relationship D. The relationship is in the shape of an inverted U Correct Answer: D

Okay, here are the Instrumentation tests in the questionnaire format.

⚙️ Instrumentation Test 1

1. What is used for EGT measurement? A. Helical bimetallic strips B. Thermistors C. Radiation pyrometry D. Thermo EMF thermocouples Correct Answer: D

2. The needle and ball of a turn indicator are both to the left of the datum. This indicates: A. a left turn with too much bank B. a left turn with too little bank C. a right turn with too little bank D. a right turn with too much bank Correct Answer: A

3. On a turn and slip indicator, needle to the left and ball to the right indicates: A. right turn not enough bank B. left turn too much bank C. left turn not enough bank D. right turn too much bank Correct Answer: C

4. Which of the following are modes of the GPWS? i. Excessive sink rate ii. Altitude loss after take-off or go-around iii. Excessive terrain closure rate iv. Deviation below glide slope v. Flight into terrain when not in landing configuration vi. Unsafe terrain clearance when not in landing configuration vii. Windshear warning A. i ii iii iv v vi vii B. ii iii v vii C. i ii iii vii D. iii iv v vi Correct Answer: A (Note: Modern EGPWS includes vi, basic GPWS typically covers i, ii, iii, iv, v, vii. Assuming the question refers to EGPWS or includes all possible modes.)

5. An aircraft is travelling at 120 kt, what angle of bank would be required for a rate one turn? A. 30 B. 12 C. 19 D. 35 Correct Answer: C (Calculation: AoB ≈ TAS/10 + 7. TAS ≈ 120 kt at low altitude. AoB ≈ 120/10 + 7 = 19)

6. What is another name for fail-active? A. Fail-soft B. Fail-operational C. Fail-safe D. Fail-passive Correct Answer: B

7. Which of the following are inputs to the central processing unit of the GPWS? i. Flaps ii. Landing gear iii. Glide slope iv. Unusual attitudes v. Radio altimeter vi. VOR A. i ii vi B. i ii iii v C. i ii iv v D. i ii iii v vi Correct Answer: B

8. What is density altitude? A. Temperature altitude B. Pressure altitude corrected for the prevailing temperature C. The altitude in the International Standard Atmosphere at which the prevailing density would be found D. Pressure altitude corrected for Total Air Temperature Correct Answer: C

9. A modern radio altimeter uses the frequency band: A. VHF 30 - 300 MHz B. SHF 3000 MHz - 30 GHz C. UHF 300 MHz - 3 GHz D. HF 3 MHz - 30 MHz Correct Answer: B

10. The true altitude of an aircraft in flight is shown from: A. the standard atmosphere B. pressure altitude C. density altitude D. temperature altitude Correct Answer: B (Note: None of the options directly represent True Altitude. Pressure altitude is the basis, corrected for non-standard temperature and pressure. The checkmark is on B, Pressure Altitude.)

11. Why must an autopilot be synchronized when you wish to disconnect? A. To ensure fail-operational landings can continue safely B. To allow automatic pitch trimming to reset C. To secure against abrupt changes in aircraft attitude D. To allow for FD coupling Correct Answer: C

12. Using a classic attitude indicator, an aircraft performs a turn through 270 at a constant angle of bank and rate of turn. The indication is: A. nose up bank right B. nose down bank left C. nose down bank right D. nose up bank left Correct Answer: A (Due to apparent precession/gyro wander in a turn).

13. A radio altimeter indicates: A. 2450 - 0 ft B. 3000 - 50 ft C. 2450 - 50 ft D. 3000 - 0 ft Correct Answer: C (Typical range is up to 2500 ft, minimum height indication around 50 ft).

14. A radio altimeter is: A. ground based and measures true altitude B. ground based and measures true height C. aircraft based and measures true altitude D. aircraft based and measures true height Correct Answer: D

15. What correction is given by TCAS? A. Turn left or right B. Climb or descend C. Contact ATC on receipt of a resolution advisory D. Climb or descend at 500 ft/min Correct Answer: B

16. An aircraft that is assessed as not being a threat would be indicated on a TCAS system as: A. a solid red square B. a solid white or cyan diamond C. a hollow white or cyan diamond D. a solid yellow circle Correct Answer: C

17. During descent through a block of airspace of constant temperature and while flying at a constant Mach No. will cause the CAS to: A. increase B. decrease C. remain constant D. increase at a rate of 198/1000 ft Correct Answer: A (Constant Mach, constant Temp => constant TAS. Descending => Increasing density => Increasing CAS for constant TAS).

18. Under conditions determined by the International Standard Atmosphere, at MSL true airspeed: A. is greater than CAS B. is less than CAS C. equals CAS D. is indeterminate due to the variation in temperature Correct Answer: C

19. If the total pressure sensor supply line leaks, and with the drain element blocked, in a non-pressurized aircraft this will cause the ASI to: A. under-read B. over-read C. over-read in the climb and under-read in the descent D. under-read in the climb and over-read in the descent Correct Answer: A

20. An aircraft is travelling at 100 kt forward speed on a 3 glide slope. What is its rate of descent? A. 500 ft/min B. 300 ft/min C. 250 ft/min D. 500 ft/sec Correct Answer: A (Calculation: RoD ≈ GS * 5 => 100 * 5 = 500 ft/min)

⚙️ Instrumentation Test 2

1. A gravity-erecting device is utilized in: A. an artificial horizon B. a directional gyroscopic indicator C. a vertical speed indicator D. a turn and slip Correct Answer: A

2. Total air temperature is ______ than static air temperature and the difference varies with ______. A. warmer altitude B. colder altitude C. warmer CAS D. colder CAS Correct Answer: C

3. The period of validity of an FMS data base is: A. 56 days B. one week C. 28 days D. varies depending on the area of operational cover Correct Answer: C

4. What does the white arc on a temperature scale indicate? A. Never exceed B. Maximum start and acceleration temperature C. Normal operating temperature D. Minimum temperature Correct Answer: C

5. A blockage occurs in the ram air source and the drain-hole. The ASI in a nonpressurized aircraft will: A. read a little low B. read a little high C. act like an altimeter D. freeze at zero Correct Answer: C

6. A rate integrating gyroscope is used in: i. inertial attitude system ii. automatic flight control systems iii. inertial navigation systems iv. rate of turn indicators A. i ii B. i iii C. i iii iv D. i ii iii Correct Answer: B

7. When accelerating on a northerly heading what does the direct reading magnetic compass indicate? A. No change B. North C. A turn to the west D. A turn to the east Correct Answer: B (Acceleration error on North/South headings causes no turn indication) Self-correction: The source checkmark is B, but acceleration error (ANDS - Accelerate North, Decelerate South) applies to East/West headings. On a Northerly heading, acceleration causes no turning error. Rechecking compass errors confirms this. The source checkmark might be incorrect.

8. In an IRS: A. the accelerometers are strapped down but the platform is gyro-stabilized B. the platform is strapped down but the accelerometers are gyro-stabilized C. accelerometers and gyros are both gyro-stabilized D. accelerometers and gyros are both strapped down Correct Answer: D

9. To convert true track to magnetic track you need: A. a deviation map B. a map with isoclinal lines C. a map with isobars D. a deviation card Correct Answer: B (Isoclinal lines show dip, Isogonal lines show variation. Variation is needed. Assuming isoclinal is a typo for isogonal.)

10. The rate of turn indicator is a very useful gyroscopic instrument. When used in conjunction with the attitude indicator it provides: A. angle of bank B. rate of turn about the yaw axis C. rate of climb D. rate of turn athwartships Correct Answer: B

11. The outputs of a flux valve are initially sent to: A. an amplifier B. an error detector C. a compass card D. a feedback loop Correct Answer: B

12. An inertial reference system is aligned when turned on so as to: A. calculate the computed trihedron with reference to the earth B. establish true and magnetic north C. establish position relative to true and magnetic north D. establish magnetic north Correct Answer: A

13. Why is there a vibration device in a pressure altimeter? i. To prevent hysteresis ii. To prevent lag in a mechanical system iii. To keep pilots happy during long flights iv. To prevent icing A. i B. i ii C. i iv D. i ii iii iv Correct Answer: B (Primarily overcomes friction/stiction, which relates to lag and hysteresis).

14. An aircraft flies into a colder airmass. This will cause the altimeter to: A. over-read B. under-read C. read the correct altitude D. the indication will depend on the hemisphere of operation Correct Answer: A ("High to Low, look out below" applies to pressure, but "Cold = Low" applies to temperature effect on true altitude vs indicated altitude. Colder air is denser, altimeter reads higher than true altitude, hence over-reads.)

15. In a solid state gyroscope the purpose of the dither motor is to: A. enhance the acceleration of the gyro at all rotational rates B. overcome laser lock C. compensate for transport wander D. stabilize the laser frequencies Correct Answer: B

16. With the aircraft weight constant but variations in airfield altitude, take-off will always be at a constant: A. equivalent airspeed B. calibrated airspeed C. ground speed D. true airspeed Correct Answer: B (Takeoff speeds are typically defined in IAS/CAS).

17. An IRS differs from an INS in that it: A. has a longer spin-up (is not affected by vertical accelerations due to gravity) B. has a shorter spin-up time and suffers from laser lock. C. does not need to correct for coriolis and central acceleration) D. does not suffer Schuler oscillations Correct Answer: B (IRS uses strapdown tech, faster alignment, Ring Laser Gyros can suffer laser lock, which dither motors prevent).

18. The rigidity (gyroscopic inertia) of a gyro rotor is improved by: A. increasing the angular momentum and concentrating the mass on the periphery of the rotor B. increasing the angular momentum and concentrating the mass at the hub of the rotor C. decreasing the angular momentum and concentrating the mass on the periphery of the rotor D. decreasing the angular momentum and concentrating the mass at the hub of the rotor Correct Answer: A

19. The errors associated with the directional indicator are: i. earth rate ii. transport wander iii. banking when pitched up iv. annual movement of the poles v. mechanical problems A. i ii iii B. i ii iv v C. i ii iii iv v D. i ii iii v Correct Answer: D

20. Which of the following correctly describes the gyroscope of a rate of turn indicator? i. 1 degree of freedom ii. 2 degrees of freedom iii. Its frame is held by two springs iv. Its spin axis is parallel to the pitch axis v. The spin axis is parallel to the yaw axis vi. The spin axis is horizontal A. i ii B. i iv v C. i iii iv D. i iii vi Correct Answer: C (1 DoF, spring restrained, spin axis parallel to lateral/pitch axis).

⚙️ Instrumentation Test 3

1. An aircraft in the northern hemisphere lands and decelerates on a westerly heading. The compass will indicate:

A. a turn north 1B. no turn will be indicated 2C. an oscillation 3D. a turn south 4Correct Answer: D 5

2. The angle formed between the directive force and the total magnetic force is called:

A. variation 6B. deviation 7C. dip 8D. isoclinal 9Correct Answer: C 10

3. The ability of a gyroscope to indicate aircraft heading is based on it having:

A. one degree of freedom in the vertical axis 11B. two degrees of freedom in the vertical axis 12C. two degrees of freedom in the horizontal 13D. one degree of freedom in the horizontal 14Correct Answer: A 15

4. If the TAS at 40000 ft is 450 kt the Mach No. is:

A. 0.815

B. 0.784

C. 0.76

D. 0.825

Correct Answer: B (LSS at 40000 ft ≈ 573.6 kt. Mach No = TAS / LSS = 450 / 573.6 ≈ 0.784)

5. The local speed of sound at mean sea level at ISA -10C is:

A. 661 kt

B. 650 kt

C. 673 kt

D. 680 kt

Correct Answer: B (Temp = 15 - 10 = 5C = 278.15 K. LSS = $38.967 \sqrt{T(K)}$ = $38.967 \sqrt{278.15}$ ≈ 650 kt)

6. The output of a double integration N/S is:

A. velocity 16B. departure 17C. distance 18D. longitude 19Correct Answer: C 20 (Integrating acceleration gives velocity, integrating velocity gives distance).

7. If a constant CAS is maintained under normal conditions in the climb what happens to the Mach No.?

A. It will decrease 21B. It will remain constant 22C. It will decrease in an isothermal layer 23D. It will increase 24Correct Answer: D 25 (Climbing at constant CAS, TAS increases. LSS decreases with altitude (in troposphere). Mach No = TAS/LSS, so Mach increases).

8. The magnetic heading reference unit has a precession rate of:

A. 1/min

B. 2/min

C. 5/min

D. 3/min

Correct Answer: B

9. A VMO/MMO alerting system contains a barometric aneroid capsule:

A. which is subjected to dynamic pressure and an airspeed capsule which is subjected to static pressure 26B. and an airspeed capsule subjected to static pressure 27C. and an airspeed capsule subjected to dynamic pressure 28D. which is subjected to static pressure and an airspeed capsule which is subjected to dynamic pressure 29Correct Answer: D 30

10. An aircraft is flying at flight level 350 at a CAS of 290 kt and a temperature deviation of ISA -10C. The TAS and MN will be:

A. TAS 498 kt Mach 0.885 31B. TAS 520 kt Mach 0.882 32C. TAS 481 kt Mach 0.855 33D. TAS 507 kt Mach 0.86 34Correct Answer: C 35 (Calculation requires flight computer or E6B for compressibility correction).

11. The EADI and the EHSI of an EFIS installation are also referred to by the manufacturers as:

A. primary display and navigation display respectively 36B. navigation display and primary display respectively 37C. EICAS and ECAM respectively 38D. ECAM and EICAS respectively 39Correct Answer: A 40

12. When measuring different pressures (low/med/high) which of the following has the three types of sensing devices in ascending order of pressure measurement?

i. Bourdon tube

ii. Bellows type

iii. Aneroid capsule

A. iii ii i 41B. i ii iii 42C. ii i iii 43D. iii i ii 44Correct Answer: A 45 (Aneroid for low pressure differences (altitude/airspeed), Bellows for medium (manifold pressure), Bourdon tube for high (hydraulic/oil pressure)).

13. Which of the following modes can be selected on an EHSI?

i. plan

ii. full ILS

iii. full VOR

iv. expanded nav

v. full ILS

vi. expanded nav

vii. full VOR

viii. expanded VOR

ix. centre map

A. i ii iv vii 46B. i iii vii viii ix 47C. ii iii vi viii ix 48D. ii iii v vii ix 49Correct Answer: C 50 (Note: Some duplication in the list suggests a copy error in the source. Common modes are Plan, Map, Full ILS, Full VOR, Expanded ILS, Expanded VOR. C includes these).

14. What is the speed of sound at 30000 ft and -40C?

A. 562 kt 51B. 595 kt 52C. 590 kt 53D. 661 kt 54Correct Answer: B 55 (Temp = -40C = 233.15 K. LSS = $38.967 \sqrt{233.15}$ ≈ 595 kt).

15. Rate of turn is affected by:

i. aircraft speed 56ii. angle of bank 57iii. aircraft weight 58A. i ii 59B. i iii 60C. ii iii 61D. none of the above 62Correct Answer: A 63 (RoT = (g * tan(AoB)) / TAS)

16. Sound is propagated at a velocity which is dependent upon:

A. barometric pressure 64B. density 65C. static pressure 66D. temperature 67Correct Answer: D 68

17. A solid state gyro is:

A. a rate gyro 69B. a rate sensor 70C. an earth gyro 71D. a tied gyro 72Correct Answer: B 73 (Detects rate of rotation using Sagnac effect, not a traditional spinning mass gyro).

18. What would the compass heading be given a true heading of 247 in an area where the variation is 8W and a compass deviation of 11E?

A. 255 74B. 244 75C. 247 76D. 266 77Correct Answer: B 78 (True (247) - Var West (add 8) = Mag (255) - Dev East (add 11) = Compass (266). Self-correction: Let's use CADET: Compass -> Add East Dev = Magnetic -> Add East Var = True. So True -> Var West (Add W) = Magnetic -> Dev East (Subtract E) = Compass. 247 + 8W = 255 (Mag). 255 - 11E = 244 (Compass). Answer B is correct.)

19. A compass swing is used to:

A. align compass north with magnetic north 79B. align compass north with true north 80C. align magnetic north with true north 81D. get true north and the lubber line aligned 82Correct Answer: A 83 (Determines deviation to align Compass North indication with Magnetic North direction).

20. Regarding magnetism, which of the following statements is correct?

i. Lines of flux run from blue pole to red pole 84

ii. Like poles repel 85

iii. Unlike poles repel 86

iv. Like poles attract 87v. Unlike poles attract 88A. i ii v 89B. i iii v 90C. ii v 91D. i iii iv 92Correct Answer: C 93 (Lines run N->S (Red->Blue), Like repel, Unlike attract).

⚙️ Instrumentation Test 4

1. In an inertial-lead VSI the source of the most pronounced error is:

A. instrument 1B. position 2C. steep turn 3D. missed approach manoeuvre 4

Correct Answer: C

2. A factor giving an error on a direct indicating compass would be:

A. crosswinds - particularly on east/west headings 5B. parallax due to oscillations of the compass rose 6C. acceleration on east/west headings 7D. turning through east/west headings 8

Correct Answer: C

3. An aircraft maintaining a constant CAS and altitude is flying from a cold airmass into warmer air. The effect of the change of temperature on the speed will be:

A. CAS will increase 9B. EAS will decrease 10C. TAS will increase 11D. TAS will decrease 12

Correct Answer: C

4. An aircraft taking off from an airfield with QNH set in the altimeter has the subscale reading erroneously set 10 hPa too low. The aircraft:

A. may lift off early with insufficient take-off speed 13B. will indicate an altitude 300 ft lower than actual altitude 14C. will indicate an altitude 300 ft higher than actual altitude 15D. will indicate the correct altitude 16

Correct Answer: B

5. Which of the following will affect a direct reading compass?

1. ferrous metals 17

2. non-ferrous metals 18

3. electrical equipment 19A. 1 only 20B. 1 & 3 21C. 1 & 2 22D. all 3 23

Correct Answer: B

6. The gravity erecting device on a vertical gyro is used on which instrument?

A. Directional gyro unit 24B. Turn indicator 25C. Artificial horizon 26D. Gyromagnetic device 27

Correct Answer: C

7. In FMS fitted aircraft the main interface between pilot and system will be provided by:

A. the automatic flight control system 28B. the multi-purpose control and display unit 29C. the flight control unit 30D. the flight management source selector 31

Correct Answer: B

8. On an EADI radio altitude is displayed:

A. digitally between 2500 ft and 100 ft 32B. on an analogue scale below 2500 ft 33C. digitally between 2500 ft and 1000 ft and thereafter as an analogue/digital display 34D. as an analogue display between 2500 ft and 1000 ft and thereafter as a digital display 35

Correct Answer: C

9. The combined Machmeter/ASI is subject to the following errors:

A. position, density, instrument, compressibility, manoeuvre induced 36B. those of the machmeter only 37C. instrument, pressure and temperature only 38D. instrument and compressibility only 39

Correct Answer: A

10. On a standard 2-dot EHSI in the en route mode each dot represents:

A. 1 NM 40B. 2 NM 41C. 5 NM 42D. 10 NM 43

Correct Answer: B

11. Wind information can be displayed in an EFIS system in which of the following modes?

A. plan map expanded ILS full VOR 44B. map centre map plan full ILS 45C. full nav full ILS map centre map 46D. full ILS full VOR map plan 47

Correct Answer: C

12. An aircraft is descending at a constant Mach number. If the aircraft is descending through an inversion layer, the CAS will:

A. remain constant 48B. increase 49C. decrease 50D. decrease then decrease more slowly 51

Correct Answer: B (Descending through inversion means temperature starts increasing. Constant Mach, increasing temp => Increasing LSS => Increasing TAS. Descending => Increasing density. Increasing TAS and increasing density => Increasing CAS).

13. Given the following information calculate the instrument error in the altimeter: Indicated altitude 2500 ft, QFE 1003 set, Airfield elevation 1000 ft, QNH 1013.

A. +20 ft 52B. +30 ft 53C. +40 ft 54D. +10 ft 55

Correct Answer: B (Pressure difference = 1013 - 1003 = 10 hPa. Altitude equivalent = 10 * 30 = 300 ft. With QFE set, altimeter should read 0 ft at airfield elevation (1000 ft). True altitude when indicating 2500 ft with QFE = 2500 + 1000 = 3500 ft. If QNH were set, it would read Pressure Altitude equivalent = 1000 ft + 300 ft = 1300 ft at airfield. Indicated 2500 ft with QFE is 1500 ft above airfield. QNH based altitude = 1500 + 1300 = 2800 ft. True Altitude needs temperature for correction. Assuming the question is simply asking for the pressure error equivalent from QFE to QNH difference relative to elevation, which isn't standard instrument error calculation. Let's assume standard calculation: Instrument error = Indicated Altitude - Corrected Altitude. Need more info for corrected altitude. Re-interpreting: Maybe it implies indicated 2500ft on the ground with QFE set? That would mean Indicated 2500 ft, Should be 0 ft -> Error +2500 ft? Unlikely. Maybe it means indicated 2500 ft when True Altitude is actually 2500 ft above MSL? QFE set indicates height above airfield. If True Alt is 2500ft, height above airfield is 1500ft. Altimeter reads 2500ft. Error = 2500 - 1500 = +1000ft? Also unlikely. The 30ft answer suggests it's related to the pressure difference. 1 hPa ≈ 30ft. QNH-QFE diff = 10hPa = 300ft. This is the difference between QNH altitude and QFE height at MSL. At 1000ft elevation, indicated 2500ft QFE means height AGL is 2500ft. Altitude AMSL = 2500+1000 = 3500ft. The pressure altitude at 3500ft AMSL with QNH 1013 is 3500ft. How 30ft error arises isn't clear from standard definitions. It might be a poorly phrased question or rely on specific diagram context not fully transferred).

14. If an aircraft, fitted with a DRMC, takes off on a westerly heading, in the northern hemisphere, the DRMC will indicate:

A. a turn to the north 56B. oscillates about west 57C. no turn 58D. a turn to south 59

Correct Answer: A (Acceleration error on West heading in N. hemisphere: ANDS - Accelerate North).

15. The rigidity (gyroscopic interia) of a gyroscope may be increased by:

A. increasing the number of gimbals and decreasing the number of planes of rotation 60B. increasing the speed of rotation and decreasing the mass of the rotor 61C. increasing the speed of rotation and increasing the mass of the rotor 62D. decreasing the speed of rotation and increasing the speed of the rotor. 63

Correct Answer: C

16. In the ILS mode, one dot on the lateral deviation scale on the EHSI indicates:

A. 1 NM 64B. 2 NM 65C. 1 66D. 2 67

Correct Answer: C (Typically 1 dot ≈ 1 for ILS/VOR modes, representing approx 0.5 deviation total full scale 2.5)

17. Select the correct statement:

A. EAS = CAS corrected for compressibility error 68B. EAS = IAS corrected for position error 69C. CAS = TAS corrected for density error 70D. TAS = EAS corrected for compressibility error 71

Correct Answer: A

18. VLO is defined as:

A. the maximum speed at which to fly with the landing gear retracted 72B. the maximum speed at which the landing gear may be retracted or extended 73C. the maximum speed at which to fly with the landing gear extended 74D. the minimum speed at which to fly with the landing gear extended 75

Correct Answer: B

19. To improve the horizontality of a compass, the magnet assembly is suspended from a point:

A. on the centre line of the magnet 76B. below the centre of gravity 77C. above the centre of gravity 78D. varying with magnetic latitude 79

Correct Answer: C

20. You are flying at a constant FL290 and constant Mach number. The total temperature increases by 5. The CAS will:

A. remain approximately constant 80B. increase by 10 kt 81C. decrease by 10 kt 82D. will increase or decrease depending on whether you are above or below ISA. 83

Correct Answer: A (Constant Mach, Increasing Temp => Increasing LSS => Increasing TAS. Constant FL => Constant Pressure Alt => Density decreases slightly with Temp increase. CAS depends on dynamic pressure ($1/2 \rho V^2$). Increasing TAS and decreasing density tend to counteract each other for CAS, often resulting in little change or a slight decrease)

⚙️ Instrumentation Test 5

1. Altitude select and altitude hold are examples of: A. inner loop functions in pitch B. manometric functions from the Air Data Computer C. interlocking functions D. outer loop functions in roll Correct Answer: B

2. What are the advantages of an IRS compared to an INS? A. Reduce spin-up time and a dither motor to prevent "lock-out". B. Reduce spin-up time and accuracy not adversely affect by "g" C. Increase accuracy and a dither motor to prevent "lock-out". D. Insensitively to "g" and reduced wander of the gyroscope. Correct Answer: B

3. If the RPM of the rotor in a turn and slip indicator is higher than normal, the turn indicator will: A. over-read the correct rate of turn B. under-read the correct rate of turn C. not indicate due to the increased rigidity D. indicate correctly Correct Answer: A

4. The ANN RNV light on an RNAV system: A. illuminates if the calculated track differs from the selected track by more than 2 NM B. illuminates if the accuracy of the calculated position falls outside predetermined limits C. illuminates if power from the aircraft bus bar has been lost and the system is operating on standby battery D. illuminates steadily after passing a waypoint in manual mode, until the next leg is programmed in Correct Answer: B

5. An autopilot delivers roll commands to the ailerons to achieve a bank angle: A. proportional to TAS, but below a specified maximum B. set bank of 25 degrees C. set bank of 30 degrees D. proportional to the deviation from the desired heading, but not exceeding a specified maximum Correct Answer: D

6. With reference to the flux valve of a remote indicating compass: A. the flux valve is pendulously mounted and is free to turn to remain aligned with the earth magnetic field B. the flux valve is not subject to acceleration errors C. the flux valve is pendulously mounted and so it is not subject to or affected by the earth's magnetic field D. the flux valve is fixed to the aircraft and senses the horizontal component of the earth's magnetic field Correct Answer: D

7. The command bars on an ADI used for autoflight command: A. heading hold, VOR radial track, ILS track, speed hold, pitch hold B. heading hold, VOR radial track, ILS track, speed hold, altitude hold, pitch hold C. heading hold, VOR radial track, altitude hold D. heading hold, VOR radial track, ILS track, altitude hold, pitch hold Correct Answer: B

8. During an approach to autoland at 1500 feet: A. off line channels are manually engaged, flare mode is armed B. localizer is controlling the roll channel, off line channels are automatically engaged and flare mode is armed C. localizer is controlling the roll channel, stabilizer is trimmed nose up and roll out is armed D. provided both localizer and glide slope signals are valid LAND 3 will be displayed Correct Answer: B

9. If only a single A/P is used to climb, cruise and approach, following a failure: A. it is fail-passive with redundancy B. it is fail-operational and will not disconnect C. it is fail-soft and will not disconnect D. it is fail-safe and will disconnect Correct Answer: D

10. At 200 ft on an autoland: A. the LOC mode is engaged in the roll channel and the G/S mode is engaged in pitch. B. the LOC mode is engaged in the roll channel and the FLARE mode is engaged in the pitch channel C. the ROLL OUT mode is engaged in the Roll channel and the G/S mode is engaged in pitch. D. the ROLL OUT mode is engaged in the Roll channel and the FLARE mode is engaged in the pitch channel Correct Answer: B

11. The term "fail passive" applied to an automatic flight control system means that in the event of failure, the system is: A. fully operational B. inoperative C. approaching decision height D. requiring a crew input Correct Answer: B

12. "LOC ARMED" lights up on the FMA part of the PFD, this means: A. localizer beam captured B. localizer beam armed and awaiting capture C. localizer alarm is on D. a/c is on localizer centre line Correct Answer: B

13. Where an alternate static source is fitted, use of this source usually leads to: A. a temporary increase in lag error B. a lower pressure error than with normal sources C. an increase in position error D. no change in position error Correct Answer: C

14. In a Schuler tuned INS, the largest unbounded errors are: A. due to acceleration errors B. track errors due to initial misalignment C. due to real wander of the platform gyroscopes D. created at the first stage of integration Correct Answer: C

15. What errors can the Air Data Computer correct for? 1. Instrument error & ram rise 2. Compressibility & density error 3. Lag & density error 4. Position & temperature error A. 1, 3 & 4 B. 1, 2, 3 & 4 C. 1, 2 & 4 D. 2 & 4 Correct Answer: C (ADCs typically correct for instrument error, position error, compressibility, density (derived from temp/pressure), and temperature (ram rise)).

16. WXR display is on: A. the captain's CRT only B. the co-pilot's CRT only C. a special screen D. on both the captain's and co-pilot's CRTs Correct Answer: D

17. During a CAT 1 ILS approach, height is indicated by: A. GPS B. radio altimeter C. marker D. barometric Correct Answer: D

18. Which of the following is the FMS normal operating condition in the cruise? A. L NAV only B. V NAV only C. L NAV or V NAV D. L NAV and V NAV Correct Answer: D

19. To obtain heading information from a gyro stabilized platform, the gyros should have: A. 1 degree of freedom and a horizontal axis B. 1 degree of freedom and a vertical axis C. 2 degrees of freedom and a horizontal axis D. 2 degrees of freedom and a vertical axis Correct Answer: A

20. Weather radar returns can be displayed in which of the following EFIS Modes? A. Plan Exp ILS Exp VOR B. Plan Exp ILS Map C. Map Exp ILS Exp VOR D. Map ILS VOR Correct Answer: C (Weather radar is commonly overlaid on Map, Expanded ILS, and Expanded VOR modes).

⚖️ Mass and Balance Test 1

1. Due to a mistake in the load sheet the aeroplane is 1000 kg heavier than you believe it to be. As a consequence: A. V1 will be later B. VMU will be later C. VR will be later D. V1, VMU, VR will all occur earlier Correct Answer: B (Increased mass increases stall speed (Vs), which directly affects VMU and VR. V1 decision speed is also affected by accelerate-stop distance, which increases with mass).

2. The datum for the balance arms has to be along the longitudinal axis: A. between the nose and the tail B. between the leading and trailing edge of the MAC C. but does not have to be between the nose and the tail D. at the fire wall Correct Answer: C

3. For a conventional light aeroplane with a tricycle undercarriage configuration, the higher the take-off mass: 1. stick forces at rotation will increase. 2. range will decrease but endurance will increase. 3. gliding range will reduce. 4. stalling speed will increase. A. all are correct B. 1 and 4 are correct C. 2, 3 and 4 are correct D. 1, 3 and 4 are correct Correct Answer: D (Higher mass increases stall speed, increases required rotation force, reduces glide range. Range generally decreases, endurance generally decreases at optimal speeds due to higher drag/power required).

4. Performance limited take-off mass may be limited by: A. Obstacle clearance and Vmcg B. Obstacle clearance C. Maximum certified take-off mass D. Climb gradient Correct Answer: D

5. Use CAP 696, MRJT 1, fig 4.9. What is the balance arm, the maximum compartment load and the running load for the most aft compartment of the fwd cargo hold? A. 421.5 cm 3305 kg 13.12 kg per inch B. 1046.5 inches 711 kg 7.18 kg per kg C. 421.5 inches 2059 kg 13.12 kg per inch D. 1046.5 m 711 kg 7.18 kg per in Correct Answer: C

6. If a compartment takes a maximum load of 500 kg, with a running load limit of 350 kg/m and a distribution load limit of 300 kg/m max, which of the following boxes, each of 500 kg, can be carried? 1. 100 cm x 110 cm x 145 cm 2. 125 cm x 135 cm x 142 cm 3. 120 cm x 140 cm x 143 cm 4. 125 cm x 135 cm x 144 cm A. Any one of the boxes if loaded with due care as to its positioning B. Either of boxes 2, 3 and 4 in any configuration C. Box 2 with its longest length perpendicular to the floor cross bearers D. Box 4 only if loaded with its longest side parallel to the main longitudinal beam Correct Answer: D (Need to check floor load (Area) and running load (Length) for each box dimension against limits. Box 4: Area=1.25*1.35=1.6875 m, Load=500/1.6875=296 kg/m (<300 OK). Running Load: 500/1.44 = 347 kg/m (<350 OK), 500/1.35 = 370 kg/m (>350 NOT OK), 500/1.25 = 400 kg/m (>350 NOT OK). So only possible if longest side (1.44m) is parallel to direction of running load limit calculation).

7. When considering CG position, it must be remembered that it is: A. set by the pilot B. set by the manufacturer C. able to exist within a range D. fixed Correct Answer: C

8. Use CAP 696, Section 4, MRJT1, as appropriate. Prior to departure an MRJT is loaded with maximum fuel of 20100 liter at an SG of 0.78. Calculate the maximum allowable traffic load that can be carried given the following data: PLTOM 67200 kg, PLLM 54200 kg, DOM 34930 kg, Taxi fuel 250 kg, Trip fuel 9250 kg, Contingency and holding fuel 850 kg, Alternate fuel 700 kg. A. 13092 kg B. 12442 kg C. 16370 kg D. 16842 kg Correct Answer: B (Fuel Mass = 20100 L * 0.78 kg/L = 15678 kg. Takeoff Fuel = Fuel Mass - Taxi Fuel = 15678 - 250 = 15428 kg. Max TOM based on fuel = ZFW + TOF. Max ZFW based on PLTOM = PLTOM - TOF = 67200 - 15428 = 51772 kg. Max ZFW based on PLLM = PLLM - TOF + Trip + Contingency + Holding = 54200 - 15428 + 9250 + 850 = 48872 kg. Limiting ZFW = 48872 kg. Max Traffic Load = Limiting ZFW - DOM = 48872 - 34930 = 13942 kg. Self-correction: Let's re-read the fuel amounts. Trip=9250, Cont+Hold=850, Alt=700. Total Required Fuel (excl Taxi) = 9250+850+700 = 10800 kg. Max Fuel loaded = 15678 kg. ZFW limited by PLTOM: Max Traffic Load = PLTOM - DOM - Takeoff Fuel = 67200 - 34930 - 15428 = 16842 kg. ZFW limited by PLLM: Max Landing Mass = PLLM = 54200 kg. Landing Mass = TOM - Trip Fuel. So Max TOM based on PLLM = PLLM + Trip Fuel = 54200 + 9250 = 63450 kg. Max Traffic Load = Max TOM based on PLLM - DOM - Takeoff Fuel = 63450 - 34930 - 15428 = 13092 kg. There's also likely a Max Structural ZFW limit not given. Assuming PLTOM is the most limiting factor for TOM (67200kg). Max Traffic Load = PLTOM - DOM - Takeoff Fuel = 67200 - 34930 - (15678 - 250) = 16842 kg. Assuming PLLM is limiting: Max TOM = 63450kg. Max Traffic Load = 63450 - 34930 - (15678-250) = 13092 kg. The checkmark is B (12442 kg). This doesn't match either structural limit calculation. There might be a Max Structural ZFW missing, which is often the most limiting factor for traffic load. If MSZFW = 47372 kg, then Max Traffic Load = 47372 - 34930 = 12442 kg. This matches B.)

9. The distance from the datum to the CG is: A. the index B. the moment C. the balance arm D. the station Correct Answer: C

10. An aircraft is flying at 1.3VS1g in order to provide an adequate margin above the low speed buffet and transonic speeds. If the 1.3VS1g speed is 180 kt CAS and the mass increases from 285000 kg to 320000 kg, what is the new 1g stalling speed? A. 146.7 kt, drag will increase and nautical mile per kg fuel burn will decrease B. 191 kt, drag will increase and range NM/kg will increase C. 191 kt, drag will increase and NM/kg fuel burn will decrease D. 147 kt Correct Answer: A (Original Vs1g = 180 / 1.3 ≈ 138.5 kt. New Vs1g = Old Vs1g * sqrt(New Mass / Old Mass) = 138.5 * sqrt(320000 / 285000) ≈ 138.5 * sqrt(1.1228) ≈ 138.5 * 1.0596 ≈ 146.7 kt. Increased mass increases drag and fuel burn per NM).

11. Exceeding the Maximum Structural Landing Mass may: A. reduce the fatigue life of the landing gear B. cause structural damage C. both a and b are correct D. no damage will occur providing the aircraft is within the performance limited landing mass Correct Answer: C

12. Individual aircraft should be weighed in an air-conditioned hangar: A. on entry into service and subsequently every 4 years B. when the effects of modifications or repairs are not known C. with the hangar doors closed and the air conditioning off D. all the above Correct Answer: D (A & B are reasons for weighing, C describes the conditions).

13. Which of the following would not affect the CG position? A. Cabin crew members performing their normal duties B. Fuel consumption during flight C. Horizontal stabilator trim setting D. Mass added or removed at the neutral point Correct Answer: C

14. The distance from the datum to the CG is: (Note: Duplicate of Q9) A. the index B. the moment C. the balance arm D. the station Correct Answer: C

15. In Mass & Balance terms, what is an index? A. A cut down version of a force B. A moment divided by a constant C. A moment divided by a mass D. A mass divided by a moment Correct Answer: B

16. The aeroplane is unstable if: A. the CG is forward B. the CG is in mid range C. the CG is on the rear limit D. the CG is behind the rear limit Correct Answer: D

17. Define the useful load: A. traffic load plus dry operating mass B. traffic load plus usable fuel mass C. dry operating mass plus usable fuel load D. that part of the traffic load which generates revenue Correct Answer: B (Useful Load = Max Ramp Mass - Basic Empty Mass).

18. If an aeroplane comes into land below its MSLM but above the PLLM for the arrival airfield: 1. airframe structural damage will occur 2. tyre temperature limits could be exceeded 3. the runway length might be inadequate 4. a go-around might not be achievable 5. brake fade could occur A. 1 and 5 only B. 3 and 4 only C. 2, 3, 4 and 5 only D. 1, 3, 4 and 5 only Correct Answer: C

19. The useful load is: (Note: Duplicate of Q17 definition) A. TOM minus fuel mass B. BEM plus fuel load C. TOM minus the DOM D. TOM minus the operating mass Correct Answer: C (Useful Load = Load Carrying Capacity = TOM - DOM).

20. Determine the position of the CG as a percentage of the MAC given that the balance arm of the CG = 92.5 cm, the leading edge = 70.8 cm and the MAC = 125 cm. A. 17.5% B. 17.7% C. 16.3% D. 17.4% Correct Answer: D (Distance from LEMAC = CG Arm - LEMAC Arm = 92.5 - 70.8 = 21.7 cm. %MAC = (Distance from LEMAC / MAC Length) * 100 = (21.7 / 125) * 100 = 17.36%).

⚖️ Mass and Balance Test 2

1. What is the zero fuel mass? A. MSTOM minus fuel to destination minus fuel to alternative airfield B. Maximum allowable mass of the aircraft with no usable fuel on board C. Operating mass minus the fuel load D. Actual loaded mass of the aircraft with no usable fuel on board

2. An aeroplane develops a serious maintenance problem shortly after take-off and has to return to its departure airfield. In order to land safely the aircraft must jettison fuel. How much fuel must be jettisoned? A. Sufficient to reduce the mass to the zero-fuel mass B. The pilot calculates the amount of fuel to jettison to reduce the mass to a safe level at or below the RLM C. The fuel system automatically stops the jettison at the RLM D. As much as the pilot feels is just in case the problem gets worse

3. If the actual take-off mass is greater than the performance limited take-off mass: A. The performance required by regulation cannot be guaranteed because the safety margins are reduced B. The safety margins are sufficient to ensure that the required performance can still be achieved C. The take-off run must be reduced D. The take-off distance must be reduced

4. The maximum structural take-off mass is: A. the maximum permissible total aeroplane mass on completion of the refuelling operation B. the maximum permissible total aeroplane mass for take-off subject to the limiting conditions at the departure airfield C. the maximum permissible total aeroplane mass for take-off but excluding fuel D. the maximum permissible total aeroplane mass at the start of the take-off run

5. The regulated take-off mass: A. is the lower of maximum structural take-off mass and the performance limited take-off mass B. is the higher of the maximum structural zero fuel mass and the performance limited take-off mass C. is the maximum structural take-off mass subject to any last-minute mass changes D. is the maximum performance limited take-off mass subject to any last-minute mass changes

6. The take-off mass is: A. the maximum permissible total aeroplane mass at the start of the take-off run B. the mass of the aeroplane including usable fuel but excluding traffic load C. the mass of the aeroplane including everything and everyone contained within it at the start of the take-off run D. the maximum mass permitted for take-off

7. The operating mass: A. is the lower of the structural mass and the performance limited mass B. is the higher of the structural mass and the performance limited mass C. is the actual mass of the aircraft on take-of D. is the dry operating mass and the fuel load

8. The basic empty mass is the mass of the aeroplane: A. plus non-standard items such as lubricating oil, fire extinguishers, emergency oxygen equipment etc. B. minus non-standard items such as lubricating oil, fire extinguishers, emergency oxygen equipment etc. C. plus standard items such as unusable fluids, fire extinguishers, emergency oxygen equipment, supplementary electronics etc. D. minus non-standard items such as unusable fluids, fire extinguishers, emergency oxygen and supplementary electronic equipment etc.

9. The term 'baggage' means: A. excess freight B. any non-human, non-animal cargo C. any freight or cargo not carried on the person D. personal property of passengers or crew members carried on an aircraft by agreement with the operator

10. An operator may: A. compute the actual mass of passengers and checked baggage by using standard masses given in tables 1, 2 and 3 B. compute the actual mass of passengers and checked baggage by weighing C. may compute the actual mass of passengers and checked baggage D. all the above

When computing the mass of passengers and baggage: 1. personal belongings and hand baggage must be included 2. infants must be classed as children if they occupy a seat 3. standard masses include infants being carried by an adult 4. table 1, table 2 and table 3 must be used as appropriate if using standard masses for passengers and freight 5. weighing must be carried out immediately prior to boarding and at an adjacent location A. 1, 2 and 5 only B. 2 and 4 only C. 1, 2, 3 and 5 only D. all the above

12. When computing the mass of passengers and baggage for an aircraft with 20 seats or more: 1. standard masses of male and female in table 1 are applicable 2. if there are thirty seats or more, the 'all adult' mass values in table 1 may be used as an alternative 3. holiday charter masses apply to table 1 and table 3 if the charter is solely intended as an exclusive holiday charter 4. the standard mass for checked baggage in table 2 is applicable A. 1, 2, 3 and 4 are correct B. 1 and 2 only are correct C. 1, 2 and 4 only are correct D. 3 and 4 only are correct

13. Refer to CAP 696 SEP. What is the CG range for normal category operations at a mass of 3000 lb? A. 79.5 inches to 87.7 inches B. 74.0 inches to 87.7 inches C. 79.5 inches to 89.5 inches D. 82.0 inches to 89.5 inches
