15. The drift down is a procedure applied: A. after aircraft depressurization B. for a visual approach to a VASI C. for an instrument approach at an airfield without an ILS D. when the engine fails above the operating altitude for one engine inoperative

16. The landing speed, Vref, for a single-engine aircraft must be not less than: A. 1.2VMCA B. 1.1Vs0 C. 1.05Vs0 D. 1.3Vs0

17. At maximum range speed in a turbojet the angle of attack is: A. the same as L/D max B. less than L/D max C. maximum D. more than L/D max (Rationale: Max range speed (Carson's speed) is slightly faster than Vmd (speed for L/D max), thus at a slightly lower angle of attack).

18. If not VMBE or VMCG limited, what would V1 be limited by? A. V2 B. Vmc C. Vr D. Vmu

19. With respect to field length limit, fill in the blanks in the follow statement. The distance to accelerate to ............, at which point an engine fails, followed by the reaction time of ............. and the ensuing deceleration to a full stop must be completed within the ............. A. VR, 2 sec, TORA B. V1 , 2 sec, ASDA C. VEF, 2 sec, TORA D. VGO, 2 sec, ASDA

20. How does the power required graph move with an increase in altitude? A. Straight up B. Straight down C. Up and to the right D. Straight across to the right

✈️ Performance Test 4

1. What procedure is likely to require V1 to be reduced? A. Improved climb procedure B. Reduced thrust take-off C. When ASDA is greater than TODA D. Take off with anti-skid inoperative (Rationale: Anti-skid inoperative increases the accelerate-stop distance. To stay within ASDA, V1 must often be reduced).

2. Two identical aircraft at different masses are descending at idle thrust. Which of the following statements correctly describes their descent characteristics? A. There is no difference between the descent characteristics of the two aeroplanes B. At a given angle of attack, the heavier aeroplane will always glide further than the lighter aeroplane C. At a given angle of attack, the lighter aeroplane will always glide further than the heavier aeroplane D. At a given angle of attack, both the vertical and the forward speeds are greater for the heavier aeroplane (Rationale: Heavier aircraft requires higher TAS for the same AoA, resulting in higher RoD and GS for the same glide angle).

3. If the performance limited take-off mass is restricted by the ASDA, which of the following actions will increase the limiting mass? A. Use a higher flap setting B. Use of clearway C. Increase V1 D. Decrease VR (Rationale: ASDA = TORA + Stopway. Clearway affects TODA, not ASDA directly. Higher flap setting decreases V1, potentially improving ASDR-limited mass. Increasing V1 worsens ASDR. Decreasing VR doesn't directly help ASDR-limited mass. The checkmark is B, but Clearway relates to TODA. A higher flap setting reducing V1 seems the most plausible way to improve ASDR-limited mass).

4. Cruising with 1 or 2 engines inoperative at high altitude, compared to all engines operative cruise, range will: A. increase B. decrease C. not change D. decrease with 1 engine inoperative, and increase with 2 engines inoperative

5. Concerning landing gear, which factors limit take-off performance? A. Brake temperature B. Tyre speed and VMBE C. Tyre temperature D. Brake wear

6. When climbing at a constant Mach number through the troposphere, TAS: A. increases B. decreases C. remains constant D. increases then decreases (Rationale: In the troposphere, temperature decreases with altitude. LSS decreases with temperature. TAS = Mach No * LSS. If Mach No is constant and LSS decreases, TAS decreases).

7. A tailwind on take-off will not affect: A. climb limit mass B. obstacle clearance C. field limit mass D. VMBE (Rationale: Tailwind increases groundspeed for a given IAS, affecting field length, obstacle clearance path over ground, and VMBE groundspeed limit. Climb gradient is an air calculation, unaffected by wind, so climb limited mass is unaffected).

8. When flying at the optimum range altitude, over time the: A. fuel consumption gradually decreases B. fuel consumption gradually increases C. fuel consumption initially decreases then gradually increases D. fuel consumption remains constant (Rationale: As fuel is burnt, weight decreases, drag decreases, requiring less thrust and thus less fuel flow to maintain optimum conditions).

9. During certification test flights for a turbojet aeroplane, the measured take-off runs from brake release to a point equidistant between the point at which VLOF is reached and the point at which the aeroplane is 35 ft above the take of surface are: 1530 m with all engines operating. 1810 m with the critical engine failure recognized at V1 , other factors remaining unchanged. What is the correct value of the take-off run? A. 1759 m B. 1810 m C. 1950 m D. 2081 m (Rationale: The certified TORR is the longest of AEO TORR * 1.15 or OEI TORR. AEO TORR * 1.15 = 1530 * 1.15 = 1759.5 m. OEI TORR = 1810 m. The longer distance is 1810 m).

10. What happens to the field limited take-off mass with runway slope? A. It increases with a downhill slope B. It is unaffected by runway slope C. It decreases with a downhill slope D. It increases with an uphill slope

11. With regards to the optimum altitude during the cruise, the aircraft is: A. always flown at the optimum altitude B. always flown 2000 ft above the optimum altitude C. flown slightly above the optimum altitude initially, descending as fuel is burnt D. flown slightly below the optimum altitude initially, climbing as fuel is burnt (Rationale: Optimum altitude increases as weight decreases. Step climbs approximate flying close to the optimum).

12. Rate of climb is: A. Excess power divided by weight B. Excess thrust divided by weight C. Maximum thrust and minimum power D. Maximum thrust and minimum drag (Rationale: Rate of Climb = (Power Available - Power Required) / Weight).

13. If a jet engine fails during take-off, before V1: A. the take-off can be continued or aborted B. the take-off should be aborted C. the take-off should be continued D. the take-off may be continued if aircraft speed is above VMCG and lies between VGO and VSTOP

14. When flying in a headwind, the speed for max range should be: A. slightly decreased B. slightly increased C. unchanged D. should be increased, or decreased depending on the strength of the wind

15. For a given aircraft mass, flying with a cost index greater than zero set will result in: A. a cruise at a slower Mach number than the best range Mach number for a given altitude B. a cruise at the maximum endurance speed C. climb at the slowest safe speed, taking into account stall and speed stability D. a cruise at a faster Mach number than the Mach number giving best air nautical miles per kg ratio for a given altitude (Rationale: Cost index balances time costs vs fuel costs. CI > 0 means time has a cost, pushing speeds higher than pure max range speed).

16. For the obstacle limited take-off mass for a Class A aircraft, turns after take-off are not permitted below 400 ft, and must not exceed: A. 15 angle of bank up to 400 ft B. 15 angle of bank below 1000 ft C. 20 angle of bank up to 400 ft D. 25 angle of bank up to 400 ft (Note: Regulations generally state no turns below 50ft/half wingspan, and limit bank angle below 400ft - often 15 degrees).

17. Vlo is defined as: A. the actual speed that the aircraft lifts of the ground B. the minimum possible speed that the aircraft could lift of the ground C. the maximum speed for landing gear operation D. the long-range cruise speed

18. The induced drag in an aeroplane: A. increases as speed increases B. is independent of speed C. decreases as speed increases D. decreases as weight increases

19. Why are step climbs used on long range fights in jet transport aircraft? A. To comply with ATC fight level constraints B. Step climbs have no significance for jet aircraft, they are used by piston aircraft C. To fly as close as possible to the optimum altitude as mass reduces D. They are only justified if the actual wind conditions differ significantly from the forecast conditions used for planning

20. In a glide (power off), how does weight affect the glide angle and the speed for best glide angle? A. Glide angle increases, speed increases B. Glide angle decreases, speed increases C. Glide angle constant, speed constant D. Glide angle constant, speed increases

✈️ Performance Test 5

1. During aircraft certification, the value of VMCG is found with nose wheel steering inoperative. This is because: A. nose wheel steering does not affect VMCG B. VMCG must be valid in both wet and dry conditions C. nose wheel steering does not work after an engine failure D. the aircraft may be operated even if the nose wheel steering is inoperative (Rationale: Certification aims for the most conservative conditions. Rudder effectiveness, which determines VMCG, can be different on wet vs dry runways without nose wheel steering).

2. How does the slush thickness affect the V1 reduction required? A. Greater reduction if thicker B. Smaller reduction if thicker C. No effect if mass is reduced D. No effect at all (Rationale: Thicker slush increases drag significantly, making acceleration difficult and stopping easier. This pushes the optimal V1 lower, meaning less reduction is needed from the dry V1 compared to thin slush where stopping might be more critical).

3. When gliding into a headwind airspeed should be: A. reduced to gust penetration speed B. the same as the max. range glide speed in still air C. lower than the max. range glide speed in still air D. higher than the max. range glide speed in still air (Rationale: To maximize ground distance (range) in a headwind, speed must be increased above best glide speed).

4. Vx is: A. Speed for best angle of climb B. Speed for best rate of climb C. Speed for obstacle clearance D. The same as Vy

5. In a balanced turn load factor is dependent on: A. radius of turn and aircraft weight B. TAS and bank angle C. radius of turn and bank angle D. bank angle only (Formula: Load Factor (n) = 1 / cos(Bank Angle))

6. If the maximum take-off mass is limited by tyre speed, what effect would a down sloping runway have? A. No effect B. Always increase the mass C. Only increase the mass if not limited by any other limitation D. Decrease the mass (Rationale: Tyre speed limit is related to groundspeed at rotation/liftoff. A downslope reduces the ground distance but doesn't change the IAS required for liftoff, and thus the corresponding groundspeed is largely unaffected by slope alone).

7. Which is true regarding a balanced field? A. Provides largest gap between net and gross margins B. Provides minimum field length required in the case of an engine failure C. Take-off distance will always be more than stopping distance D. Distances will remain equal, even if engine failure speed is changed (Rationale: Balanced field length occurs when Accelerate-Stop Distance equals Accelerate-Go Distance for a given V1).

8. If V1 is found to be lower than VMCG, which of the following statements will be true? A. VMCG must be reduced B. V1 must be increased to at least VMCG C. VR must be reduced D. V2 must be reduced (Rationale: V1 cannot be less than VMCG, as the aircraft must be controllable on the ground with the critical engine failed at the point of decision).

9. During take-off an aircraft is affected by windshear. If the wind changes from a headwind to a tailwind the effect will be: A. TOD increasing and ASD decreasing, and the calculated V2 being too fast B. TOD and ASD decreasing, and the calculated V2 being too fast C. TOD and ASD remaining constant, if the calculated speeds are used D. TOD and ASD increasing, if the calculated speeds are used (Rationale: Sudden tailwind decreases airspeed, reducing lift and performance, potentially leading to stall or undershoot. V2 calculated for headwind conditions would be too fast relative to the new lower IAS).

10. The reduced thrust take-off procedure may not be used when: A. runway wet B. after dark C. temperature varies by more than 10C from ISA D. anti-skid unserviceable (Rationale: Reduced thrust calculations assume normal stopping capability. Anti-skid inoperative reduces stopping capability).

11. How is fuel consumption affected by the C of G position, in terms of air nautical miles per kg? A. Increases with a forward C of G B. Decreases with an aft C of G C. Decreases with a forward C of G D. Fuel consumption is not affected by the C of G position (Rationale: Forward CG requires more tail-down force (trim drag), increasing overall drag and fuel consumption, thus decreasing NM/kg).

12. What factor must be applied to the landing distance available at the destination aerodrome to determine the landing performance of a turbojet aircraft on a dry runway? A. 1.43 B. 1.15 C. 0.60 D. 0.70 (Rationale: Landing Distance Required (LDR) must be no more than 60% of the Landing Distance Available (LDA). LDR = LDA * 0.60).

13. During the certification flight testing of a twin engine turbojet aeroplane the actual measured Landing Distances are: 1100 m on a dry runway, 1300 m on a wet runway. What are the values that will be entered into the AFM for the LDR on dry and wet runways? A. 1833 m, 2167 m B. 1265 m, 1495 m C. 1650 m, 1733 m D. 1833 m, 1495 m *(Calculation: Dry LDR = Actual Dry / 0.6 = 1100 / 0.6 = 1833 m. Wet LDR = Dry LDR * 1.15 = 1833 * 1.15 = 2108 m. Self-correction: The source checkmark is D (1833m, 1495m). 1833m is correct for Dry. Let's check the wet calculation. Wet LDR must also be demonstrated, actual wet was 1300m. Factored Wet LDR = Actual Wet / 0.6 = 1300 / 0.6 = 2167m. However, regulations also state that the required wet LDA must be at least 115% of the required dry LDA. Required Dry LDA = Dry LDR / 0.6 = 1100 / 0.6 = 1833m. Required Wet LDA = 1.15 * Required Dry LDA = 1.15 * 1833 = 2108m. The LDR published in the AFM is the factored distance. So Dry LDR = 1833m. Wet LDR = Higher of (Actual Wet / 0.6) or (1.15 * Dry LDR). Wet LDR = Higher of (1300/0.6 = 2167m) or (1.15 * 1833 = 2108m). So Wet LDR = 2167m. Answer A seems correct based on this. The marked answer D has 1495m for wet. 1495m = 1300 * 1.15. This suggests they are factoring the actual wet distance by 1.15, which isn't the standard procedure. Assuming the checkmark D is correct despite regulatory interpretation, Dry=1833m, Wet=1495m).

14. Climbing in the troposphere at a constant TAS: A. Mach number increases B. Mach number decreases C. CAS increases D. IAS increases (Rationale: Climbing => Temperature decreases => LSS decreases. Mach No = TAS / LSS. Constant TAS, decreasing LSS => Increasing Mach number).

15. At MSL, in ISA conditions Climb gradient = 6%. What would the climb gradient be if: Pressure altitude 1000 ft, Temperature 17C, Engine anti-ice on, Wing anti-ice on (- 0.2% engine anti-ice, - 0.1% wing anti-ice, 0.2% per 1000 ft pressure altitude, 0.1 % per 1C ISA deviation) A. 5.1% B. 6.3% C. 3.8% D. 5.5% (Calculation: ISA Temp @ 1000ft = 15 - (21) = 13C. ISA Dev = 17 - 13 = +4C. Gradient Change = -0.2 (Eng AI) - 0.1 (Wing AI) - (0.2 * 1) (Alt) - (0.1 * 4) (Temp) = -0.2 - 0.1 - 0.2 - 0.4 = -0.9%. New Gradient = 6% - 0.9% = 5.1%)*.

16. What does density altitude signify? A. Pressure altitude B. Flight levels C. ISA altitude D. An accurate indication of aircraft and engine performance

17. Which denotes the stall speed in the landing configuration? A. Vs0 B. Vs1 C. Vs D. Vs1g

18. Which of the following combinations most reduces the take-off and climb performance of an aircraft? A. High temperature and high pressure B. Low temperature and high pressure C. Low temperature and low pressure D. High temperature and low pressure (Rationale: High density altitude reduces performance. High temp and low pressure both contribute to high density altitude).

19. When in a gliding maneuver, in order to achieve maximum endurance the aircraft should be flown at: A. the speed for max. lift B. the speed for min. drag C. the speed for max. lift / drag D. the speed for min. power (Rationale: Max endurance (minimum sink rate) occurs at the speed for minimum power required).

20. With a downward sloping runway: A. V1 will increase B. V1 will decrease C. VR will increase D. VR will decrease (Rationale: Downslope helps acceleration (reducing accelerate-go distance) but hinders stopping (increasing accelerate-stop distance). To balance the field length, V1 is typically reduced).

✈️ Principles of Flight Test 1

1. The Principle of Continuity states that in a streamtube of decreasing cross-sectional area, the speed of a subsonic and incompressible airflow will:

A. remain the same 1B. decrease 2C. increase 3D. sonic 4

2. The Principle of Continuity states that in a tube of increasing cross sectional area, the speed of a subsonic and incompressible airflow will:

A. remain the same 5B. decrease 6C. sonic 7D. increase 8

3. Static pressure acts:

A. parallel to airflow 9B. parallel to dynamic pressure 10C. in all directions 11D. downwards 12

4. Consider a uniform flow of air at velocity V in a streamtube. If the temperature of the air in the tube is raised:

A. the mass flow remains constant and velocity V decreases 13B. the mass flow decreases and the velocity V remains constant 14C. the mass flow increases and the velocity V remains constant 15D. the mass flow remains constant and the velocity V will increase 16

5. As subsonic air flows through a convergent duct: (i) static pressure (ii) velocity

A. (i) increases and (ii) decreases 17B. (i) increases and (ii) increases 18C. (i) decreases and (ii) decreases 19D. (i) decreases and (ii) increases 20

6. Which of the following is the equation for power?

A. N/m 21B. Nm/s 22C. Pa/s squared 23D. Kg/m/s squared 24

7. Bernoullis Theorem states:

A. dynamic pressure increases and static pressure increases 25B. dynamic pressure increases and static pressure decreases 26C. dynamic pressure is maximum at stagnation point 27D. there is zero pressure at zero dynamic pressure 28

8. The difference between IAS and TAS will:

A. increase with decreasing temperature 29B. increase with increasing density 30C. remain constant at all times 31D. increase with increasing altitude 32

9. Equivalent Air Speed (EAS) is:

A. IAS corrected for compressibility and position/instrument error 33B. lower than the speed of the undisturbed airstream around the aircraft 34C. lower than IAS at ISA altitudes below sea level 35D. equal to IAS, multiplied by air density at sea level 36

10. At a constant CAS when flying below sea level an aircraft will have:

A. a higher TAS than at sea level 37B. a lower TAS than at sea level at ISA conditions 38C. the same TAS as at sea level 39D. the same TAS, but an increased IAS 40

11. In accordance with Bernoullis Theorem, where PT = Total Pressure, PS = Static pressure and q = Dynamic pressure:

A. PT + PS = q 41B. PT = PS - q 42C. PT - PS = q 43D. PS + PT = q 44

12. In a subsonic flow venturi, the relationship between the total pressure, static pressure and dynamic pressure of undisturbed air and air in the throat will be: (i) Dynamic pressure will be constant, static pressure will decrease. (ii) Total pressure will be constant, dynamic pressure will increase.

A. both (i) and (ii) are correct 45B. (i) is correct but (ii) is incorrect 46C. (i) and (ii) are correct 47D. (i) and (ii) are incorrect 48

(Note: Statement (i) is incorrect, dynamic pressure increases. Statement (ii) is correct, total pressure remains constant (ideally) and dynamic pressure increases. Therefore B should be the answer, but the checkmark is on D).

✈️ Principles of Flight Test 2

1. A symmetrical aerofoil section at CL = 0 will produce?

A. A negative (nose-down) pitching moment. 49B. A positive (nose-up) pitching moment. 50C. Zero pitching moment. 51D. No aerodynamic force. 52

2. Which of the following most accurately describes the airflow which causes wing tip vortices?

A. From the root to the tip on the top surface and from the tip to the root on the bottom surface over the wing tip 53B. From the root to the tip on the top surface and from the tip to the root on the bottom surface over the trailing edge 54C. From the tip to the root on the top surface and from the root to the tip on the bottom surface over the trailing edge 55D. From the tip to the root on the top surface and from the root to the tip on the bottom surface over the wing tip 56

3. With increasing angle of attack, the stagnation point moves ............. and the point of lowest pressure moves ...............

A. down, forward 57B. up, aft 58C. down, aft 59D. up, forward 60

4. The formula for lift is:

A. L = W 61B. L = 2 rho V squared S CL 62C. L = 1/2 rho V squared S CL 63D. L = rho V S CL 64

(Formula: $L = \frac{1}{2} \rho V^2 S C_L$)

5. Angle of attack is the angle between:

A. undisturbed airflow and chord line. 65B. undisturbed airflow and mean camber line. 66C. local airflow and chord line. 67D. local airflow and mean camber line 68

6. If IAS is doubled, by which of the following factors should the original CL be multiplied to maintain level flight?

A. 0.25 69B. 0.5 70C. 2.0 71D. 4.0 72

(Rationale: Lift must remain constant (equal to weight). $L = \frac{1}{2} \rho V^2 S C_L$. If V doubles, $V^2$ increases by 4. To keep L constant, $C_L$ must decrease by a factor of 4, i.e., multiplied by 0.25).

7. When considering the lift and drag forces on an aerofoil section:

A. they are only normal to each other at one angle of attack. 73B. they both depend on the pressure distribution on the aerofoil section. 74C. they vary linearly. 75D. lift is proportional to drag. 76

8. When considering the coefficient of lift and angle of attack of aerofoil sections:

A. a symmetrical section at zero angle of attack will produce a positive coefficient of lift. 77B. an asymmetrical section at zero angle of attack will produce zero coefficient of lift. 78C. a symmetrical section at zero angle of attack will produce zero coefficient of lift. 79D. aerofoil section symmetry has no effect on lift coefficient. 80

9. When considering an angle of attack versus coefficient of lift graph for a cambered aerofoil, where does the lift curve intersect the vertical CL axis?

A. above the origin 81B. below the origin 82C. at the point of origin 83D. to the left of the origin 84

10. Where does the lift act on the wing?

A. Suction 85B. Always forward of the CG 86C. Centre of Gravity 87D. Centre of Pressure 88

11. Which of the following is the correct definition of aspect ratio?

A. Span divided by tip chord 89B. Chord divided by span 90C. Span divided by mean chord 91D. Chord divided by span, measured at the 25% chord position 92

(Formula: $AR = b / \bar{c}$ or $AR = b^2 / S$, where b=span, $\bar{c}$=mean chord, S=wing area)

12. On entering ground effect:

A. more thrust is required 93B. induced drag decreases 94C. the stalling speed increases 95D. parasite drag decreases 96

13. Which of the following is the cause of wing tip vortices?

A. Air spilling from the top surface to the bottom surface at the wing tip 97B. Air spilling from the bottom surface to the top surface at the wing tip 98C. Air spilling from the bottom surface to the top surface at the left wing tip and from the top surface to the bottom surface at the right wing tip 99D. Spanwise flow vector from the tip to the root on the bottom surface of the wing 100

14. An aircraft is flying straight and level, if density halves, aerodynamic drag will:

A. increase by a factor of four 101B. increase by a factor of two 102C. decrease by a factor of two 103D. decrease by a factor of four 104

(Rationale: For constant IAS in level flight, Lift is constant. $L = \frac{1}{2} \rho V^2 S C_L$. If $\rho$ halves, $V^2$ must double, meaning $V$ increases by $\sqrt{2}$. Drag $D = \frac{1}{2} \rho V^2 S C_D$. Assuming $C_D$ changes negligibly, D changes proportionally to $\rho V^2$. Since $\rho$ halved and $V^2$ doubled, the product $\rho V^2$ is unchanged. Therefore, drag should remain constant. However, the checkmark is C. This would be true if TAS remained constant, not IAS. If TAS is constant and density halves, drag $D = \frac{1}{2} \rho (TAS)^2 S C_D$ would halve. Assuming the question implies constant TAS).

15. High aspect ratio:

A. reduces parasite drag 105B. reduces induced drag 106C. increases stalling speed 107D. increases manoeuvrability 108

16. CDi is proportional to which of the following?

A. CLMAX 109B. CL squared 110C. the square root of CL 111D. CL 112

(Formula: $C_{Di} = C_L^2 / (\pi \cdot AR \cdot e)$)

17. If IAS is reduced from 150 kt to 75 kt in straight and level flight, the induced drag will change by a factor of:

A. 16 113B. 8 114C. 4 115D. 2 116

(Rationale: In level flight, L=W=constant. $L \propto V^2 C_L$. If V halves, $V^2$ decreases by 4, so $C_L$ must increase by 4. $D_i \propto C_L^2 / V^2$. $C_L^2$ increases by $4^2=16$. $V^2$ decreases by 4. $D_i$ changes by $16 / (1/4)$ = $16 * 4$ = 64? Let's use $D_i \propto 1/V^2$ for constant lift. If V halves, $V^2$ decreases by 4. $D_i$ increases by 4. The checkmark is A=16. Induced Drag $D_i = \frac{1}{2} \rho V^2 S C_{Di}$. We know $C_{Di} \propto C_L^2$ and $C_L \propto 1/V^2$ (for level flight). So $C_{Di} \propto (1/V^2)^2 = 1/V^4$. Substitute this into the drag equation: $D_i \propto V^2 \cdot (1/V^4) = 1/V^2$. So if V halves, Di increases by $1 / (1/2)^2 = 1 / (1/4) = 4$. Checkmark A=16 seems incorrect unless related to power).

18. What is interference drag?

A. Airflow retardation over the aircraft structure due to surface irregularities 117B. Drag caused by high total pressure at the leading edges when compared to the lower pressure present at the trailing edge 118C. Drag caused by the generation of lift 119D. Drag due to the interaction of individual boundary layers at the junction of aircraft major components 120

19. At a constant IAS, induced drag is affected by:

A. aircraft weight 121B. changes in thrust 122C. angle between chord line and longitudinal axis 123D. wing location 124

(Rationale: Constant IAS means $V^2$ term is constant. $D_i \propto C_L^2$. In level flight $L=W$, so $C_L \propto W$. Thus $D_i \propto W^2$. Changing weight affects induced drag).

20. On the approach to land, ground effect will begin to be felt at:

A. twice the wingspan above the ground 125B. one wingspan above the ground 126 (Correction: Marked answer in source is B, but standard texts often state effect begins around one wingspan).

C. when the angle of attack is increased 127D. upon elevator deflection

✈️ Principles of Flight Test 3

1. What is the cause of induced angle of attack?

A. Downwash from trailing edge in the vicinity of the wing tips

B. Change in flow from effective angle of attack

C. The upward inclination of the free stream flow around the wing tips

D. Wing downwash altering the angle at which the airflow meets the tailplane

2. What phenomena causes induced drag?

A. Wing tip vortices

B. Wing tanks

C. The increased pressure at the leading edge

D. The spanwise flow, inward below the wing and outward above

3. When considering the properties of a laminar and turbulent boundary layer, which of the following statements is correct?

A. Friction drag is the same

B. Friction drag higher in laminar

C. Friction drag higher in turbulent

D. Separation occurs earlier in turbulent

4. The boundary layer is:

A. the layer between upper and lower surfaces

B. the thin layer of air over an aerofoil where the air is slowed by viscosity

C. the layer below the transition point

D. the wing tip vortex

5. CDi is the ratio of?

A. (CL) squared to S

B. (CL) squared to AR

C. rho V squared

D. rho V squared S

(Rationale: $C_{Di} = C_L^2 / (\pi \cdot AR \cdot e)$. It's directly proportional to $C_L^2$ and inversely proportional to Aspect Ratio (AR)).

6. Which of the following is a characteristic of laminar flow boundary layer?

A. Constant velocity

B. Constant temperature

C. No flow normal to the surface

D. No vortices

7. Stall speed in a turn is proportional to:

A. lift

B. weight

C. the square root of the load factor

D. TAS squared

(Formula: $V_{S(turn)} = V_{S(level)} \times \sqrt{n}$, where n = load factor).

8. When the undercarriage is lowered in flight:

A. form drag will increase and the aircrafts nose-down pitching moment will be unchanged

B. induced drag will increase and the aircrafts nose-down pitching moment will increase

C. form drag will increase and the aircrafts nose-down pitching moment will increase

D. induced drag will decrease and the aircrafts nose-down pitching moment will increase

9. In recovery from a spin:

A. ailerons should be kept neutral

B. airspeed increases

C. ailerons are used to stop the spin

D. rudder and ailerons are used against the direction of spin rotation

10. If the stalling speed in a 15 degree bank turn is 60 kt, what would the stall speed be in a 45 degree bank?

A. 83 kt

B. 70 kt

C. 85 kt

D. 60 kt

(Calculation: $n_{15} = 1/\cos(15) \approx 1.035$. $n_{45} = 1/\cos(45) \approx 1.414$. $V_{S(level)} = 60 / \sqrt{1.035} \approx 58.9$ kt. $V_{S(45)} = 58.9 \times \sqrt{1.414} \approx 70.0$ kt).

11. If a jet aircraft is at 60 degrees bank angle during a constant altitude turn, the stall speed will be:

A. 1.60 greater

B. 1.19 greater

C. 1.41 greater

D. 2.00 greater

(Calculation: $n_{60} = 1/\cos(60) = 2$. Stall speed increases by $\sqrt{n} = \sqrt{2} \approx 1.414$).

12. Which statement about induced drag and tip vortices is correct?

A. Vortex generators diminish tip vortices.

B. Flow on upper and lower wing surfaces is towards the tip.

C. They both decrease at high angle of attack.

D. On the upper surface there is a component of flow towards the root, whilst on the lower surface it is towards the tip.

13. The stalling speed of an aircraft in straight and level flight is 80 kt. What is the stalling speed in a level turn with a load factor of 2.25?

A. 120 kt

B. 150 kt

C. 81 kt

D. 100 kt

(Calculation: $V_{S(turn)} = V_{S(level)} \times \sqrt{n} = 80 \times \sqrt{2.25} = 80 \times 1.5 = 120$ kt).

14. When compared to a laminar boundary layer:

A. a turbulent boundary layer has more kinetic energy

B. a turbulent boundary layer is thinner

C. less skin friction is generated by a turbulent layer

D. a turbulent boundary layer is more likely to separate

15. A jet aircraft flying at high altitude encounters severe turbulence without encountering high speed buffet. If the aircraft decelerates, what type of stall could occur first?

A. Low speed stall

B. Accelerated stall

C. Deep stall

D. Shock stall

16. If VS is 100 kt in straight and level flight, during a 45 bank turn VS will be:

A. 100 kt

B. 140 kt

C. 80 kt

D. 119 kt

(Calculation: $V_{S(45)} = 100 \times \sqrt{1/\cos(45)} = 100 \times \sqrt{1.414} \approx 118.9$ kt).

17. When considering the aerodynamic forces acting on an aerofoil section:

A. lift and drag increase linearly with an increase in angle of attack

B. lift and drag act normal to each other only at one angle of attack

C. lift and drag coefficients are equal at 4 degrees angle of attack

D. lift increases linearly and drag increases exponentially with an increase in angle of attack

18. Which of the following is the correct formula for drag?

A. rho V squared CL S

B. rho V (CL) squared S

C. rho V squared AR CD S

D. rho V squared CD S

(Formula: $D = \frac{1}{2} \rho V^2 S C_D$)

19. In level flight at 1.4VS what is the approximate bank angle at which stall will occur?

A. 44 degrees

B. 30 degrees

C. 60 degrees

D. 32 degrees

(Calculation: Stall occurs at speed V when required $n = (V/V_S)^2 = (1.4V_S/V_S)^2 = 1.96$. $n=1/\cos(\text{bank})$. Bank = $\arccos(1/1.96) \approx 59.3^\circ$).

20. A swept wing aircraft stalls and the wake contacts the horizontal tail. What would be the stall behaviour?

A. Nose down

B. Nose up and/or elevator ineffectiveness

C. Tendency to increase speed after stall

D. Nose up

Okay, here is Principles of Flight Test 4 in the questionnaire format.

✈️ Principles of Flight Test 4

1. What is load factor? A. 1 / Bank angle B. Weight / Lift C. Lift / Weight D. Weight / Wing area

2. The CP on a swept wing aircraft will move forward due to: A. boundary layer fences and spanwise flow B. tip stall of the wing C. flow separation at the root due to spanwise flow D. change in wing angle of incidence

3. What is a high speed stall? A. Separation of the airflow due to shock wave formation B. A stall caused by increasing the load factor (g) during a manoeuvre C. A stall due to decreasing CLMAX at speeds above M 0.4 D. Excessive dynamic pressure causing airflow separation

4. The effect of tropical rain on drag and stall speed would be to: A. increase drag and increase stall speed B. increase drag and decrease stall speed C. decrease drag and increase stall speed D. decrease drag and decrease stall speed

5. Stalling speed increases when: A. recovering from a steep dive B. the aircraft is subjected to minor altitude changes, i.e. 0 to 10000 ft C. the aircraft weight decreases D. flaps are deployed (Rationale: Pulling out of a dive increases the load factor, which increases stall speed).

6. VS is 100 kt at n = 1. What will the stall speed be at n = 2? A. 200 kt B. 119 kt C. 141 kt D. 100 kt (Calculation: kt).

7. Which of the following aircraft designs would be most prone to super stall? A. T-tail B. Swept forward wing C. Swept-back wing D. Pod mounted engines beneath the wing (Note: While T-tails are associated with deep stall, swept-back wings are also prone due to tip stall characteristics affecting the tailplane. The checkmark is on C).

8. Which of the following is the most important result/problem caused by ice formation? A. Increased drag B. Increased weight C. Blockage of the controls D. Reduction in CLMAX

9. What causes deep stall in a swept-back wing? A. CP moves aft B. CP moves forward C. Root stall D. Spanwise flow from tip to root on wing upper surface (Rationale: Tip stall occurs first on swept wings, causing the CP to move forward, leading to a pitch-up tendency. Deep stall specifically involves the wake blanking the tailplane).

10. What are the effects of tropical rain on: (i) CLMAX (ii) Drag A. (i) increase (ii) decrease B. (i) decrease (ii) increase C. (i) increase (ii) increase D. (i) decrease (ii) decrease

11. The IAS of a stall: A. increases with high altitude, more flaps and slats B. may increase with increasing altitude, especially high altitude, forward CG and icing C. decreases with forward CG and increasing altitude D. altitude never affects stall speed IAS

12. Vortex generators: A. take energy from the laminar flow to induce boundary layer separation B. use free stream flow to induce laminar flow C. prevent spanwise flow D. use free stream flow to increase energy in the turbulent boundary layer

13. What causes a swept wing aircraft to pitch-up at the stall? A. Negative camber at the root B. Separated airflow at the root C. Spanwise flow causing the tips to stall first D. Strong lateral stability

14. A stick pusher will: A. Activate at a certain angle of attack and pull the control column backwards B. Activate at a certain angle of attack and push the stick forward C. Activate at a certain IAS and vibrate the stick D. Activate at a certain IAS and push the stick forward

15. Which of the following combination of characteristics would be most likely make an aircraft susceptible to deep stall? A. Swept wing and wing mounted engines B. Swept wing and a T-tail C. Straight wing and wing mounted engines D. Straight wing and a T-tail

16. Which of the following is the correct designation of stall speed in the landing configuration? A. VS1g B. VS1 C. VS0 D. VSL

17. What effect on stall speed do the following have? A. Increased anhedral increases stall speed B. Fitting a T-tail will reduce stall speed C. Increasing sweepback decreases stall speed D. Decreasing sweep angle decreases stall speed

18. The lift formula is: A. L=CL Rho V S B. L=CL 2 Rho V S C. L=CL Rho V S D. L=CD Rho V S

19. What happens to the stall speed with flaps down, when compared to flaps up? A. Increase B. Decrease C. Remain the same

20. What influence does the CG being on the forward limit have on VS and the stall angle? A. VS increases, stall angle remains constant B. VS increases, stall angle increases C. VS decreases, stall angle remains constant D. VS decreases, stall angle decreases (Rationale: Forward CG requires more tail-down force, increasing overall lift needed, thus increasing Vs. The critical angle of attack for the wing itself doesn't change significantly).

✈️ Principles of Flight Test 5

1. Which stall has the greatest angle of attack?

A. Low speed stall

B. High speed stall (shock stall)

C. Deep stall

D. Accelerated stall

2. Which of the following is used to activate a stall warning device?

A. Movement of the CP

B. Movement of the CG

C. Movement of the stagnation point

D. A reduction in dynamic pressure

(Rationale: Stall warning vanes or ports are positioned to detect the stagnation point moving close to them as angle of attack increases towards the stall).

3. An aircraft has trailing edge flap positions of 0, 15, 30 and 45 degrees plus slats can be deployed. What will have the greatest negative influence on CL/ CD?

A. Deploying slats

B. 0 - 15 flaps

C. 15 - 30 flaps

D. 30 - 45 flaps

(Rationale: High flap settings significantly increase drag ($C_D$) more than they increase lift ($C_L$), thus reducing the L/D ratio ($C_L/C_D$)).

4. What is pitch angle?

A. The angle between the chord line and the horizontal plane

B. The angle between the longitudinal axis and the horizontal plane

C. The angle between the longitudinal axis and the relative airflow

D. The angle between the chord line and the relative airflow

5. How does a plain flap increase CL?

A. Increases camber

B. Increases angle of attack

C. Changes position of CP

D. Decreases the Aspect Ratio

6. When flying straight and level in 1g flight, slightly below maximum all up weight, a basic stall warning system (flapper switch) activates at 75 kt IAS and the aircraft stalls at 68 kt IAS. Under the same conditions at maximum all up weight the margin between stall warning and stall will:

A. increase because increasing weight increases the 1g stall speed

B. decrease because the 1g stall speed is an IAS

C. decrease because increasing weight increases the 1g stall speed

D. remain the same because increased weight increases the IAS that corresponds to a particular angle of attack

(Rationale: Stall warning activates at a specific angle of attack, and stall occurs at the critical angle of attack. While the IAS values for these angles increase with weight, the difference in angle of attack (and thus the IAS margin percentage) remains relatively constant).

7. The CG of an aeroplane is in a fixed position forward of the neutral point. Speed changes cause a departure from the trimmed speed. The aeroplane is:

A. statically unstable

B. statically stable

C. statically neutral

D. dynamically unstable

(Rationale: CG forward of the neutral point provides static longitudinal stability, meaning the aircraft tends to return towards its trimmed speed after a disturbance).

8. Why are slats generally used in combination with flaps during take-off and landing?

A. Because flaps extended gives a large decrease in stall speed with relatively less drag

B. Because slats extended provides a better view from the cockpit than flaps extended

C. Because slats extended provides a better view from the cockpit than flaps extended

D. Because slats extended gives a large decrease in stall speed with relatively less drag

(Note: Double identical answer C & D).

9. If flaps are extended in level flight:

A. lift and drag increase

B. CLMAX increases

C. CL and drag increase

D. CL increases

(Rationale: Extending flaps increases the maximum lift coefficient ($C_{L_{MAX}}$) and also increases both lift and drag for a given angle of attack).

10. What is the effect of an aft shift of the CG on (1) static longitudinal stability and (2) the required control deflection for a given pitch change?

A. (1) reduces (2) increases

B. (1) increases (2) increases

C. (1) increases (2) reduces

D. (1) reduces (2) reduces

11. For an aircraft flying straight and level at constant IAS, when flaps are deployed the induced drag:

A. increases

B. decreases

C. increases or decreases depending on the aircraft

D. stays the same

(Rationale: Induced drag $D_i \propto L^2 / (\rho V^2 S)$. In level flight L=W. Constant IAS means $V^2$ is roughly constant. Deploying flaps increases $C_L$ for a given AoA but allows flight at a lower AoA to maintain L=W. $D_i$ depends on $C_L^2$. The change in $C_L$ required to maintain level flight at constant IAS when flaps are deployed means the induced drag may change, likely increasing. However, the checkmark is D).

12. Which statement is correct?

A. The stick force stability can be zero or slightly positive for civil transport aeroplanes

B. The stick force per g must have both upper and lower limits in order to assure acceptable control characteristics

C. If the slope of the fe-n line becomes negative, generally speaking this is not a problem for control of an aeroplane

D. The stick force per g can only be corrected by means of electronic devices (stability augmentation) in the case of an unacceptable value

13. Which of the following is the speed that would activate the stick shaker?

A. 1.5 VS

B. 1.15 VS

C. 1.2 VS

D. Above VS

(Rationale: Stick shaker activates at a speed margin above the actual stall speed VS, typically around 1.05 to 1.1 VS).

14. In order to maintain straight and level flight when trailing edge flaps are retracted, the angle of attack must:

A. be increased or decreased depending on type of flap

B. be decreased

C. be increased

D. stay the same because the lift requirement will be the same

15. Extending the flaps while maintaining a constant angle of attack (all other factors constant):

A. the aircraft will sink suddenly

B. the aircraft will yaw

C. the aircraft will climb

D. the aircraft will maintain level flight

(Rationale: Extending flaps increases lift at a constant angle of attack).

16. A leading edge slot:

A. increases the energy of the boundary layer and decreases the critical angle of attack

B. increases the wing leading edge radius by rotating forward and down from its stowed position on the bottom side of the wing leading edge

C. deploys automatically under the influence of increased stagnation pressure at high angles of attack / low IAS

D. increases the energy of the boundary layer and increases the maximum angle of attack

17. How is the pitching moment affected if flaps are deployed in straight and level flight?

A. Pitch up

B. Pitch down

C. Depends on CG position

(Note: Flaps typically cause a pitch-down moment due to increased downwash on the tail and aft movement of the wing CP, but the overall effect depends on aircraft design and CG).

18. If the angle of attack is maintained constant, what happens to the coefficient of lift when flaps are deployed?

A. Increases

B. Decreases

C. Changes with the square of IAS

D. Remains constant because angle of attack remains the same

19. With a swept wing the nose-up phenomena is caused by:

A. deploying lift augmentation devices

B. wing fences

C. wing tip stall

D. leading edge devices

20. Static longitudinal stability is the tendency of an aircraft to:

A. nose-down pitching moment when encountering an up gust

B. nose-up pitching moment with a speed change at a constant angle of attack

C. nose-down pitching moment with a speed change at a constant angle of attack

D. nose-up moment when encountering an up gust

(Rationale: Stability means it resists disturbances. An up gust increases AoA; a stable aircraft will pitch nose-down to return to its trimmed AoA).

📋 Operational Procedures Test 1

1. When refuelling is being conducted with passengers embarking or disembarking: A. refuelling is strictly prohibited whilst passengers are embarking/ disembarking B. all flight crew must be on board C. communications shall be maintained by ground crew and qualified crew on board D. the stairs shall be fully extended

2. What must be ensured with respect to navigation equipment? A. The failure of one piece does not affect another B. All navigation equipment must be serviceable at the start of flight C. All equipment must conform to ICAO specifications D. If one piece of equipment fails there must be a spare available

3. Supplemental oxygen is used to: A. provide oxygen to passengers who might require it, following decompression B. provide oxygen to passengers following decompression if the cabin altitude exceeds 10000 ft C. provide oxygen to flight crew following decompression D. augment first aid oxygen following decompression

4. Who is responsible for checking the quantity and security of the cargo on board? A. The company's cargo technicians B. The captain C. The mechanic on board, or in his absence the co-pilot D. The operator

5. Who is the operator to provide an operations manual for? A. Operations staff B. All company personnel C. Only for flight crew D. For the Authority

6. Information concerning evacuation procedures can be found in the: A. OM B. AFM C. journey logbook D. OFP

7. To act as co-pilot for take-off or landing you must have: A. acted as PIC or co-pilot on type in the last 90 days B. acted as PIC or co-pilot on type in the last 30 days C. acted as PIC or co-pilot on type in the last 60 days D. been at the controls for landing in the same type recently

8. What is the co-pilot currency requirement? A. 3 flights in the last 90 days B. 3 take-offs and landings in the last 60 days C. At the controls for 3 take-offs and landings within the previous 90 days D. 3 take-offs and landings in the previous 90 days

9. One shall not initiate any flight made in accordance with instrument flight rules unless the available information indicates that the conditions at the aerodrome of intended destination and destination alternate (if one is required) are, at the predicted time of: A. take-off equal to or better than the minimum conditions required for aerodrome use B. arrival, and for a reasonable time before and after such a predicted time, equal to minimum conditions required for aerodrome use C. arrival equal to or better than the minimum conditions required for aerodrome use D. arrival better than the minimum conditions required for aerodrome use

10. Where is the Minimum Equipment List? A. Appended to the AFM B. In the OM C. In the maintenance documents D. In the operations room

11. FDRs must keep data and parameters for at least the last: A. 30 hours of operation B. 48 hours of operation C. 10 hours of operation D. the whole flight

12. The period of validity for an operator's certificate is: A. one year renewable B. indefinite C. three years renewable D. five years renewable

13. When are flight crew allowed to leave their stations? A. In the performance of their duties B. At any time specified by the OM C. When having lunch D. Only when the captain allows it

14. The recent experience conditions of a captain assigned to a flight on an aircraft by an operator must not be less than: A. 6 take-offs and 6 landings as pilot in command on this type of aircraft during the last 90 days B. 3 take-offs and 3 landings as pilot in command on this type of aircraft during the last 6 months C. 6 take-offs and 6 landings as pilot in command on this type of aircraft during the last 6 months D. 3 take-offs and 3 landings as pilot in command on this type of aircraft during the last 90 days

15. The Minimum Equipment List (MEL) is established by the: A. airline operator B. manufacturer C. aeronautical Authority the airline operator depends on D. Civil Aviation Authority of the European states

16. When are life jackets required? A. 100 NM from land B. 300 NM from land C. 50 NM from land D. 400 NM from land

17. Aeroplanes with a take-off mass greater than 5700 kg shall be fitted with an independent automatically operated emergency power supply to operate and illuminate the artificial horizon for: A. 15 mins B. 30 mins C. 60 mins D. 2 hrs

18. When do you not need a destination alternate aerodrome? A. If there is a reasonable certainty that at the ETA at the destination aerodrome and a reasonable time before and after you can expect VMC B. If the flight time is more than 6 hours C. If the flight time is less than 1 hour D. If your operator deems the weather to be suitable for a visual landing

19. A piece of equipment on your public transport aeroplane fails while you are still parked. The reference document you use to decide on the procedure to follow is the: A. OM chapter "Abnormal and Emergency procedures" B. AFM C. OPS D. MEL

20. Where is the general information and policy on fuel located? A. Operations Manual Part B B. Operations Manual Part A C. Aircraft Flight Manual D. Maintenance Manual

📋 Operational Procedures Test 2

1. What is the requirement for the carriage of life rafts? A. 30 mins or 120 NM whichever is less B. 50 NM from land C. 120 mins or 400 NM whichever is less D. 60 mins flying time at the one engine out cruise speed

9. The crew members must use their seatbelts: A. only during take-off and landing B. while at their station C. from take-off to landing D. only during take-off and landing and whenever necessary by the commander in the interest of safety

10. On an NDB approach with an MDH of 360 ft and a required RVR of 1500 m and a reported met vis of 2500 m, when can you start an approach? i.e. which is most correct? A. When the cloud base is above the system minimum B. With any cloud base C. When the cloud base is above 36 ft D. When the cloud base report is received (Rationale: For non-precision approaches, cloud base is not the limiting factor for commencing the approach; required visibility/RVR is).

11. The MEL is drawn up by the: A. operator and may be more restrictive than the MMEL B. operator and may be less restrictive than the MMEL C. manufacturer and may be more restrictive than the MMEL D. manufacturer and may be less restrictive than the MMEL

12. On an ILS, you are told that the weather has dropped below company minima. When must you abort the approach? A. Start of the glide slope descent B. Before passing the outer marker or equivalent position C. Before passing the middle marker D. Before reaching decision height

13. Which communications systems must be carried for IFR flights? A. 2 independent VHF boxes or one VHF and one HF B. One VHF box C. Two independent VHF boxes D. One VHF box and one HF box

14. Who provides the operations personnel with the OM and the amendments to keep it up to date? A. Aircraft manufacturer B. ATS authority of the State of Registry C. Aircraft operator D. Owner of aircraft

15. What is the oxygen requirement for the crew and 100% of the passengers in an unpressurized aircraft? A. 10000 ft B. 11000 ft C. 12000 ft D. 13000 ft (Rationale: Above 13000ft, oxygen required for all occupants for entire time above 13000ft).

19. Above what altitude are quick-donning masks required? A. 25000 ft B. 15000 ft C. 10000 ft D. 32000 ft

20. Destination alternate for a turbojet - what is the required fuel overhead? A. 30 minutes at cruise speed B. 30 minutes at 1500 ft in standard conditions C. 2 hours at 1500 ft in standard conditions D. 30 minutes at endurance speed (Rationale: This refers to the final reserve fuel requirement).

📋 Operational Procedures Test 3

1. At the alternate aerodrome, the commander of a turbojet engine aeroplane should have a fuel quantity (final reserve) sufficient for flying during: A. 30 minutes at holding flight speed at 1500 ft B. 45 minutes at holding flight speed at 1500 ft C. 30 minutes at cruising speed D. 45 minutes at cruising speed

This list is prepared by: A. the operator, and it is included in the Operations Manual B. the manufacturer, and it is included in the Operations Manual C. the manufacturer, and it is included in the Aircraft Flight Manual D. the operator, and it is included in the Aircraft Flight Manual

Significant obstacles in the missed approach area 4. Dimensions and characteristics of the runway 5. 📋 Operational Procedures Test 4

1. Which of the following are not required to be carried on each flight? A. CofA B. NOTAMS and AIS briefing material C. European Health Insurance Card (EHIC) for all crew D. Third party insurance certificate

6. Each flight is subject to a preliminary file collecting a certain amount of information. The operator will see that this file is kept on ground. It particularly contains: 1. the weather conditions for the day including the weather forecast at destination 2. one copy of the operational flight plan and, if required, the weight and balance sheet 3. copies of the relevant aircraft's technical log 4. the en route NOTAM documentation when specifically issued by the operator 5. special loads notification 6. charts The combination regrouping all the correct statements is: A. 1, 3 & 5 B. 2, 3, 4 & 5 C. 2 & 4 D. 1, 2, 3, 4, 5 & 6

ILS (LLZ only) - MDH 200 ft D. VOR/DME - MDH 300 ft (Note: The absolute lowest MDH depends on specific approach design, but generally, VOR approaches allow for lower minima than NDB, and LLZ can be lower still. The checkmark is B).

13. Coverage of permanently illuminated white lights at the rear of the aircraft is: A. 140 B. 70 C. 110 D. 220 (Rationale: Tail navigation light coverage is typically 70 left and 70 right of the tail, totaling 140).

When threshold and mid-runway RVRs are greater than 800 m B. When all 3 RVRs are greater than 800 m C. When the met viz is greater than 800 m. RVR is for precision approaches only D. When threshold RVR is greater than 800 m

2. What is the Cat IIIB RVR minimum? A. 50 m B. 100 m C. 200 m D. 250 m

3. What is the minimum horizontal visibility for a Cat D aircraft on a circling approach? A. 1500 m B. 1600 m C. 2400 m D. 3600 m

4. A category I precision approach (CAT I) is an approach which may be carried out with an RVR/Visibility of not less than: A. 800 m B. 550 m C. 350 m D. 500 m

5. OPS 1.465 (VFR operating minima), establishes that, the operator shall ensure about VFR flights, that: A. for conducted VFR flights in airspace F, vertical distance from clouds is 250 m at least B. Special VFR flights are not commenced when visibility is less than 3 km C. for conducted VFR flights in airspace B, horizontal distance from clouds is 1000 m at least D. for conducted VFR flights in airspace E, flight visibility at and above 3050 m (10000 ft) is 5 km at least (clear of cloud)

6. What is Vat? A. Vso x 1.3 B. Vs1g x 1.3 C. The lesser of Vso or Vs1g D. Vso x 1.23

7. The Cat I minimum decision height is: A. no decision height B. 50 ft C. 100 ft D. 200 ft

8. When establishing an instrument approach procedure, 5 aircraft categories according to their speed at the threshold (Vat) are established. This speed is equal to the stalling speed in landing configuration multiplied by: A. 1.1 B. 1.23 C. 1.15 D. 1.3

9. For VFR flight (in a cat C aircraft) what is the minimum horizontal visibility below 10000 ft? A. 8 km B. 5 km C. 1500 m D. 300 m

10. The information to be considered for a non-precision approach is: 1. horizontal visibility 2. ceiling 3. minimum descent altitude 4. decision altitude A. 1, 2 & 4 B. 1 & 3 C. 1 & 4 D. 1, 2 & 3

11. What is the minimum crew rest period before flight? A. 12 hours when operating away from home base B. 13 hours, reducing by 30 minutes for every sector after the 3rd sector in a day C. 10 hours when operating from home base D. 12 hours when operating from home base

12. Who could be nominated as Senior Cabin Crew? A. Any flight crew B. Cabin crew with more than one year experience C. Any cabin crew over the age of 18 D. Cabin crew as long as they are not qualified on more than 3 types or variants

13. According to OPS 1.430 (Aerodrome Operating Minima) a Category IIIA approach has a Decision Height of less than 100 ft and a minimum RVR (Runway Visual Range) of: A. 175 m B. 250 m C. 300 m D. 200 m

14. Aircraft are categorized according to their threshold speeds, multiplied by a factor. What aircraft category corresponds to a range of speeds 141 kt - 165 kt? A. Aeroplane category B B. Aeroplane category E C. Aeroplane category D D. Aeroplane category C

15. What are the rules regarding OPCs? A. Can be completed in the simulator, but no passengers to be carried B. Can be completed in the aircraft but only if the aircraft is certified by the Authority as a suitable substitute for the simulator C. Can be completed in the simulator but only if the simulator is certified by the Authority D. Can be completed in conjunction with a line check

16. What are the threshold speeds defining a Cat B aircraft? A. < 91 kt B. 91 - 120 kt C. 121 - 140 kt D. 141 - 165 kt

17. What are the limits on crew duty? A. 190 hours in a year, 60 duty hours in any seven consecutive days B. 900 block hours in a year, 60 block hours in any consecutive 7 days C. 900 block hours in a year, 100 block hours in any consecutive 28 days D. 190 block hours in any consecutive 7 days, 900 block hours in any consecutive 28 days

18. What is the take-off RVR limit for a Cat A aeroplane, when high intensity centre line lights and edge lights are on and the crew is IFR qualified and approved? A. 150 m if threshold RVR is available B. 150 m C. 200 m D. 250 m

19. When is MDH referenced to the threshold as opposed to the aerodrome elevation? A. The threshold is more than 2 m above the ARP B. The threshold is less than 2 m above the ARP C. The threshold is less than 2 m below the ARP D. The threshold is more than 2 m below the ARP

📡 Radio Navigation Test 1

1. An aircraft flies from a VOR at 61N 013W to 58N 013W. The variation at the beacon is 13W and the variation at the aircraft is 5W. What radial is the aircraft on? A. 013 B. 005 C. 193 D. 187 (Calculation: Aircraft is South of the VOR (same longitude). True bearing FROM VOR to Aircraft is 180(T). Radial = Magnetic Bearing FROM VOR. Use Variation at VOR: Radial = 180(T) + 13W = 193(M)).

2. Determine which of the following statements concerning atmospheric ionization are correct: 1. The highest levels of ionization will be experienced in low latitudes 2. Ionization levels increase linearly with increasing altitude 3. The lowest levels of ionization occur about midnight 4. The E-layer is higher by night than by day because the ionization levels are lower at night A. statements 1, 2 and 3 are correct B. statements 1, 3 and 4 are correct C. statements 2 and 4 are correct D. statements 1 and 4 are correct (Rationale: Ionization is highest during the day due to solar radiation, and generally higher at higher altitudes, but not linearly. The E-layer does tend to be higher/weaker at night. Low latitudes near the equator experience high ionization. Lowest levels occur before sunrise. Statement 1 is generally true (highest overall radiation near equator). Statement 4 is true. Statement 3 is false (lowest before sunrise). Statement 2 is false (not linear). Checkmark is D (1 and 4 correct)).

3. The accuracy of VDF Class A bearing is: A. +/- 10 B. +/- 5 C. +/- 2 D. +/- 1

4. The Doppler effect is used in some navigation systems to determine .........., it causes a .......... in frequency of a radio transmission if the transmitter and receiver are moving ......... A. position, change, towards each other B. relative motion, decrease, apart C. the distance, increase, at the same speed D. relative motion, increase, apart

5. The accuracy of ADF by day and excluding compass error is: A. +/-1 B. +/-2 C. +/-5 D. +/-10

6. The principal propagation path employed in an NDB/ADF system is: A. sky wave B. surface wave C. direct wave D. ducted wave

7. When converting VOR and ADF bearings to true, the variation at the should be used for VOR and at the for ADF A. aircraft aircraft B. aircraft station C. station aircraft D. station station

8. The maximum range an ATC facility at 1369 ft AMSL can provide a service to an aircraft at FL350 is: A. 276 NM B. 200 NM C. 224 NM D. 238 NM (Calculation: Range (NM) ≈ 1.23 * (sqrt(H1_ft) + sqrt(H2_ft)). Range ≈ 1.23 * (sqrt(1369) + sqrt(35000)) ≈ 1.23 * (37 + 187) ≈ 1.23 * 224 ≈ 275.5 NM).

9. ADF quadrantal error is caused by: A. static build-up on the airframe and St. Elmos Fire B. the aircrafts major electrical axis, the fuselage, reflecting and re-radiating the incoming NDB transmissions C. station interference and/or night effect D. NDB signals speeding up and bending as they cross from a land to water propagation path

10. Which wavelength corresponds to a frequency of 5035 MHz? A. 5.96 mm B. 5.96 cm C. 5.96 m D. 59.6 cm (Calculation: Wavelength = Speed of Light / Frequency = (3 * 10^8 m/s) / (5035 * 10^6 Hz) ≈ 0.0596 m = 5.96 cm).

11. An NDB has emission designator N0NA1A this will require the use of the BFO for: A. tuning B. identification C. identification and monitoring D. tuning, identification and monitoring (Rationale: N0N A1A indicates unmodulated carrier wave with Morse code keying - requires BFO to hear the tone).

12. The pilot of an aircraft flying at FL240 is 250 NM from a VOR at 16 ft AMSL which he selects. He receives no signal from the VOR. This is because: A. the VOR is unserviceable B. the range of VOR is limited to 200 NM C. the aircraft is beyond line of sight range D. there are abnormal atmospheric conditions (Calculation: Max Range ≈ 1.23 * (sqrt(24000) + sqrt(16)) ≈ 1.23 * (155 + 4) ≈ 1.23 * 159 ≈ 195 NM. 250 NM is beyond this range).

13. Coastal refraction error is maximum when the NDB signal crosses the coast at: A. a coastal beacon at an acute angle B. an inland beacon at an acute angle C. a coastal beacon perpendicular to the coast D. an inland beacon perpendicular to the coast

14. The ADF error which will cause the needle to hunt (i.e. oscillate around the correct bearing) is: A. night effect B. CB static C. station interference D. coastal refraction

15. The Doppler effect is: A. the change in frequency caused by the movement of a transmitter and receiver B. the change in frequency caused by the movement of a receiver C. the change in frequency caused by the movement of a transmitter D. the change in frequency caused by the relative movement between a transmitter and receiver

16. A class B VDF bearing will have an accuracy of: A. 2 B. 10 C. 5 D. 1

17. The VDF term meaning true bearing from the station is: A. QDM B. QUJ C. QDR D. QTE

18. The phase difference measured at the aircraft from a VOR is 235. The bearing of the beacon from the aircraft is: A. 055 B. 235 C. 145 D. 325 (Rationale: Phase difference = Radial (magnetic bearing FROM beacon). Radial = 235. Bearing TO beacon = 235 - 180 = 055).

19. An error applicable to VDF would be: A. synchronous transmission B. scalloping C. selective availability D. garbling

20. The principle of operation of VOR is: A. bearing by lobe comparison B. bearing by frequency comparison C. bearing by searchlight principle D. bearing by phase comparison

📡 Radio Navigation Test 2

1. When flying downwind abeam the upwind end of the runway the indications from the ILS on the CDI will be: A. in the correct sense for the localizer and no glide path signal B. erratic on both localizer and glide path C. erratic on the localizer and in the correct sense on the glide path D. no localizer signal and in the correct sense for glide path

2. MLS has 200 channels available in the frequency band: A. 108 112 MHz B. 329 335 MHz C. 960 1215 MHz D. 5031 5090 MHz

3. The time interval between the transmission of a pulse and receipt of the echo from a target is 925.5 microseconds. The range of the target is: A. 37.5 NM B. 75 NM C. 150 NM D. 300 NM (Calculation: Radar mile = 12.34 microseconds/NM (round trip). Range = Time / 12.34 = 925.5 / 12.34 ≈ 75 NM).

4. The best resolution will be obtained from: A. a narrow beam width and narrow pulse width B. a wide beam width and narrow pulse width C. a narrow beam width and wide pulse width D. a wide beam width and wide pulse width

5. The SSR code to select when the aircraft is being unlawfully interfered with is: A. 7600 B. 7700 C. 7500 D. 7400

6. A precision approach runway CAT II is an instrument runway served by ILS and visual aids intended for operations down to: A. a RVR of 550 meters and a DH of not less than 200 ft B. a RVR of 200 meters and a DH of not less than 100 ft C. a RVR of 250 meters and a DH of not less than 200 ft D. a RVR of 300-450 meters and a DH of not less than 100 ft

7. The type of radar which has no minimum range restriction is: A. primary CW radar B. primary pulsed radar C. secondary CW radar D. secondary pulsed radar

8. An advantage of a slotted antenna (planar array) over a parabolic reflector are: A. side lobes removed B. 360 scan without any rotation requirement C. less power required D. high gain

9. Refer to Appendix A, diagram B. What are the indications on the VOR/ILS display? A. 030, TO, Fly Right B. 030, TO, Fly Left C. 210, FROM Fly Right D. 210, FROM, Fly Left (Note: Appendix A diagrams not provided, answer based on checkmark).

10. Flying an ILS approach the equipment senses that the 90 Hz modulation predominates on both the localizer and the glide path. The indications the pilot will see are: A. fly left and fly up B. fly left and fly down C. fly right and fly up D. fly right and fly down

11. On a colour AWR display, the heaviest precipitation will be displayed in: A. amber B. red C. yellow D. blue

12. The coverage of the approach azimuth and elevation of a MLS is: A. +/-20 to 40 NM B. +/-20 to 20 NM C. +/-40 to 40 NM D. +/-40 to 20 NM

13. A radar transmitting on 600 MHz has a PRF of 300 pps and an aerial rotation rate of 5 rpm. This radar will be: A. an area surveillance radar B. an aerodrome surface movement radar C. an aerodrome surveillance radar D. a terminal area radar

14. The AWR operating frequency is: A. 9375 MHz B. 9375 GHz C. 937.5 MHz D. 93.75 GHz

15. On an ILS approach, using a 3 glide path, the height of an aircraft, ground speed 160 kt, at 3.5 NM from touchdown should be: A. 800 ft B. 1050 ft C. 900 ft D. 1500 ft (Calculation: Height ≈ Distance (NM) * Angle * 100 ≈ 3.5 * 3 * 100 ≈ 1050 ft).

16. The AWR frequency is selected because it gives: A. good returns from water droplets B. good returns from turbulence C. good penetration of cloud D. good returns from water vapour

17. The azimuth coverage of a 3 glide path is: A. +/-35 to 17 NM B. +/-10 to 25 NM C. +/-8 to 10 NM D. +/-10 to 8 NM

18. The maximum theoretical range of a radar is determined by: A. power B. PW C. beamwidth D. PRF

19. In SSR the aircraft replies on .............. MHz and the ground station interrogates on ................. MHz A. 1030 1090 B. 1090 1030 C. 1030 1030 D. 1090 1090

20. A full MLS system comprises a DME and: A. 4 elements multiplexing on 2 frequencies B. 4 elements multiplexing on one frequency C. 2 elements using 2 frequencies D. 2 elements multiplexing on one frequency

📡 Radio Navigation Test 3

1. If the signal from an SV is lost during an aircraft manoeuvre:

A. can be modified by the flight crew to meet the route requirements 5B. can be modified every 28 days 6C. can only be read by the flight crew 7D. cannot be accessed by the flight crew 8

A. 15 minutes 9B. 2.5 minutes 10C. 12.5 minutes 11D. 5 minutes 12

A. in the nose cone to give maximum forward range 13B. as close to the fore/aft centre line as possible 14C. on top of the fuselage close to the wings 15D. close to each wing tip to compensate for manoeuvre errors 16

10. The model of the earth used for GPS is:

A. WGS90 37B. PZ84 38C. PZ90 39D. WGS84 40

11. EGNOS provides a WAAS by determining the errors in ................ and broadcasting these errors to receivers using ................

A. X, Y & Z coordinates geostationary satellites 41B. X, Y & Z coordinates pseudolites 42C. SV range geostationary satellites 43D. SV range pseudolites 44

12. If the aircraft DME interrogates a ground transponder on a frequency of 1199 MHz, it will receive replies on:

A. 1199 MHz 45B. 1073 MHz 46C. 1262 MHz 47D. 1136 MHz 48

(Rationale: DME uses paired frequencies separated by 63 MHz. Aircraft transmits high, receives low (X channels) or transmits low, receives high (Y channels). 1199 MHz is high band. Reply is 1199 - 63 = 1136 MHz).

13. The purpose of the PRN codes in NAVSTAR/GPS is to:

A. identify the satellites 49B. synchronize the receiver clocks with the SV clocks 50C. pass navigation and system data to the receiver 51D. all of the above 52

A. 3 53B. 4 54C. 5 55D. 6 56

[Image E is missing, based on checkmark]

A. 360(M) 57B. 130(M) 58C. 360(T) 59D. 130(T) 60

16. The principle error in GNSS is:

A. ionospheric propagation 61B. GDOP 62C. receiver clock error 63D. SV ephemeris error 64

17. The number of SVs required to produce a 3D fix is:

A. 3 65B. 4 66C. 5 67D. 6 68

18. Refer to Appendix A. Which diagram shows the MAP display?

[Images A-F missing, based on checkmark]

A. Diagram A 69B. Diagram B 70C. Diagram C 71D. Diagram D 72E. Diagram E 73F. Diagram F 74

19. The DME in an aircraft at FL630 measures a slant range of 16 NM from a ground station at 1225 ft AMSL. The plan range is:

A. 12.5 NM 75B. 19 NM 76C. 16 NM 77D. 10.5 NM 78

(Calculation: Height difference = 63000 - 1225 = 61775 ft. Height diff (NM) = 61775 / 6076 ≈ 10.17 NM. Plan Range = $\sqrt{\text{Slant}^2 - \text{Height}^2} = \sqrt{16^2 - 10.17^2} = \sqrt{256 - 103.4} = \sqrt{152.6} \approx 12.35$ NM).

20. The altitude read-out at the ground station from a mode C response will give the aircraft altitude within:

A. 300 ft 79B. 100 ft 80C. 500 ft 81D. 50 ft 82

(Note: Mode C reports altitude in 100ft increments based on standard pressure. The accuracy required by ATC systems is often within +/- 50ft or better relative to the reported value, but the reporting resolution is 100ft. The question likely asks about the displayed accuracy/tolerance).
