📡 Radio Navigation Test 4

1. Refer to Appendix A, diagram C. What is the symbol designated DFC which is coloured cyan? [Image E is missing, based on checkmark] A. an in-use VORTAC B. an available VORTAC C. an in-use NDB D. an available NDB

2. The middle marker is usually located at a range of ................., with an audio frequency of ................ and illuminates the ................. light. A. 4-6 NM 1300 Hz white B. 1 km 400 Hz white C. 1 km 1300 Hz amber D. 1 km 400 Hz amber

3. The main advantage of a continuous wave radar over a pulsed radar is: A. more complex equipment but better resolution and accuracy B. removes the minimum range restriction C. smaller more compact equipment D. permits measurement of Doppler in addition to improved range and bearing

4. For a conventional VOR a phase difference of 090 would be achieved by flying............... from the beacon: A. west B. north C. east D. south (Rationale: Phase difference equals the magnetic radial FROM the beacon).

5. The ILS glide slope transmitter generates false glide slope signals: A. above the true glide slope B. below the true glide slope C. either side of the localizer D. outside the coverage area

6. At a range of 200 NM from a VOR, if there is an error of 1, how far off the centre line is the aircraft? A. 3.5 NM B. 1.75 NM C. 7 NM D. 1 NM (Calculation: Distance off ≈ (Angle Error * Distance) / 60 = (1 * 200) / 60 ≈ 3.33 NM).

7. The coverage of the ILS glide slope with respect to the localizer centre line is: A. +/-10 to 8 NM B. +/-10 to 25 NM C. +/-8 to 10 NM D. +/-35 to 17 NM

8. Refer to appendix A, diagram F. What is the required track? [Image F is missing, based on checkmark] A. 165 B. 173 C. 157 D. 130

9. The principle of operation of the ILS localizer transmitter is that it transmits two overlapping lobes on: A. different frequencies with different phases B. the same frequency with different phases C. the same frequency with different amplitude modulations D. different frequencies with different amplitude modulations

10. The amplitude modulation of the ILS outer marker is ............... and it illuminates the................light in the cockpit. A. 400 Hz blue B. 1300 Hz amber C. 400 Hz amber D. 1300 Hz blue

11. Which of the following systems use pulse technique? 1. secondary surveillance radar 2. airborne weather radar 3. distance measuring equipment 4. primary radar A. all the above B. 2 and 4 only C. 2 only D. 1 and 3 only

12. On an ILS approach you receive more of the 90 Hz modulation than the 150 Hz modulation. The action you should take is: A. fly left and up B. fly left and down C. fly right and up D. fly right and down (Rationale: 90Hz predominates = Fly Right (Localizer), Fly Down (Glide Path))

13. In which frequency band does ILS operate? A. UHF/VHF B. VHF C. SHF D. VLF (Rationale: Localizer is VHF, Glide Slope is UHF).

14. Distance on MLS is measured by: A. measuring the time taken for the primary radar pulse to travel from the MLS transmitter to the aircraft receiver B. measuring the time taken for the secondary radar pulse to travel from the MLS transmitter to the aircraft receiver C. phase comparison between the azimuth and elevation beams D. co-located DME

15. The coverage of MLS is ............... either side of the centre line to a distance of............... A. 40 40 NM B. 40 20 NM C. 20 20 NM D. 20 40 NM

16. In which band does the ILS glide path operate? A. metric B. centimetric C. decimetric D. hectometric (Rationale: UHF band corresponds to decimetric wavelengths).

17. Refer to Appendix A, diagram A. What is the deviation from the required track? [Image A is missing, based on checkmark] A. 3 NM left B. 3 NM right C. 8 left D. 8 right

18. The definition of a radar display will be best with: A. narrow beamwidth and narrow pulsewidth B. narrow beamwidth and wide pulsewidth C. wide beamwidth and narrow pulsewidth D. wide beamwidth and wide pulsewidth

19. Primary radar operates on the principle of: A. transponder interrogation B. pulse technique C. phase comparison D. continuous wave emission

20. The best radar for measuring very short ranges is: A. a continuous wave primary radar B. a pulsed secondary radar C. a pulsed primary radar D. a continuous wave secondary radar

📡 Radio Navigation Test 5

1. NAVSTAR GPS receiver clock error is removed by: A. regular auto-synchronization with the satellite clocks B. adjusting the pseudo-ranges to determine the error C. synchronization with the satellite clocks on initialization D. having an appropriate atomic time standard within the receiver

2. The main advantage of a slotted scanner is: A. reduces side lobes and directs more energy into the main beam B. removes the need for azimuth slaving C. side lobe suppression D. can produce simultaneous map and weather information

3. The advantages of SSR mode S are: A. improved resolution, TCAS B. data link, reduced voice communications C. TCAS, no RT communications D. better resolution, selective interrogation

4. The DME IDENT signal consists of a Morse code transmission every: A. 30-40 seconds at a pitch of 1350 Hz B. 30-40 seconds at a pitch of 1020 Hz C. 10-15 seconds at a pitch of 1350 Hz D. 10-15 seconds at a pitch of 1020 Hz

5. The positioning of a GNSS aerial on an aircraft is: A. in the fin B. on the fuselage as close as possible to the receiver C. on top of the fuselage close to the centre of gravity D. under the fuselage

6. The use of the AWR on the ground is: A. not permitted B. permitted provided reduced power is used C. permitted provided special precautions are taken to safeguard personnel and equipment D. only permitted to assist movement in low visibility conditions

7. The airborne weather radar (AWR) cannot detect: A. snow B. moderate rain C. dry hail D. wet hail (Note: While AWR detects precipitation, dry snow reflects poorly. Dry hail also reflects poorly compared to wet hail/rain. The checkmark is A).

8. What are the ground components of MLS? A. Separate azimuth and elevation antennae with DME B. Separate azimuth and elevation antennae with middle and outer markers C. Combined azimuth and elevation antennae with DME D. Combined azimuth and elevation antennae with middle and outer markers

9. Area navigation is: A. one which enables the aircraft to navigate on any desired flight path within the coverage of appropriate ground based navigation aids or within the specified limits of self-contained on-board systems or a combination of the two B. one which enables the aircraft to navigate on any desired flight path within the coverage of appropriate ground based navigation aids or within the specified limits of self-contained on-board systems but not a combination of the two C. one which enables the aircraft to navigate on any desired flight path within the coverage of appropriate ground based navigation aids only D. one which enables the aircraft to navigate on any desired flight path within the specified limits of self-contained on-board systems

10. Which is the most suitable radar for measuring short ranges? A. Millimetric pulse B. Continuous wave primary C. Centimetric pulse D. Continuous wave secondary

11. The PRN codes are used to: A. determine the time taken for the signal to reach the receiver B. differentiate between signals from different satellites C. pass navigation information to the receiver D. pass clock correction data to the receiver

12. Refer to Appendix A, diagram D. What is the track deviation? [Image D is missing, based on checkmark] A. 0.8 NM left B. 0.8 NM right C. 8 NM left D. 8 NM right

13. The SSR ground transceiver interrogates on ................ and receives responses on ................ A. 1030 MHz 1030 MHz B. 1030 MHz 1090 MHz C. 1090 MHz 1030 MHz D. 1090 MHz 1090 MHz

14. The accuracy of SSR mode C altitude as displayed to the air traffic controller is: A. +/-25 ft B. +/-50 ft C. +/-75 ft D. +/-100 ft

15. Concerning NAVSTAR/GPS orbits, which of the following statements is correct? A. The inclination of the orbits is 55 with an orbital period of 12 hours B. The inclination of the orbits is 55 with an orbital period of 24 hours C. The orbits are geostationary to provide global coverage D. The orbits are inclined at 65 with an orbital period of 11 hours 15 minutes

16. Why is a secondary radar display free from weather clutter? A. The frequencies are too low to detect water droplets B. The frequencies are too high to detect water droplets C. Moving target indication cancels out weather returns D. Weather returns are filtered out because they do not originate from transponders

17. The frequency used for airborne weather radar is: A. 9375 MHz B. 937.5 MHz C. 93.75 GHz D. 9375 GHz

18. The vertical position provided by SSR mode C is referenced to: A. QNH unless QFE is in use B. 1013.25 hPa C. QNH D. WGS84 datum

19. The EHSI is showing 5 fly right with a TO indication. The aircraft heading is 280(M) and the required track is 270. The radial is: A. 275 B. 265 C. 085 D. 095 (Calculation: Required track = 270(M). TO indication means aircraft is flying towards the station on approx reciprocal radial. Deviation 5 right means aircraft is 5 left of track. Actual track = 270 - 5 = 265(M) TO the station. Radial FROM = 265 - 180 = 085. The checkmark is D=095. Let's re-read: Fly RIGHT 5. Required Track = 270. Aircraft is LEFT of track. Current track TO station = 270 - 5 = 265. Radial FROM = 265 - 180 = 085. If Required Track meant the Radial FROM, then 270 radial. Fly right 5 means current radial is 270-5 = 265. If required track meant the bearing TO, = 270. Fly right 5 means current bearing TO = 270+5=275. Radial FROM = 275-180=095. This matches D).

20. The contents of the navigation and systems message from NAVSTAR/GPS SVs include: A. satellite clock error, almanac data, ionospheric propagation information B. satellite clock error, almanac data, satellite position error C. position accuracy verification, satellite clock time and clock error D. ionospheric propagation information, X, Y & Z coordinates and corrections, satellite clock time and error
